601 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Finnegan


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


280 Pa. Super. 584; 421 A.2d 1086; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3143


April 16, 1980, Submitted  
September 26, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied February 26, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 156 April Term, 1979, Appeal from the Judgments of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Nos. CC7800913A and CC7802735A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which convicted and sentenced him on four counts of promoting prostitution, and single counts of resisting arrest and criminal conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, on two occasions, was the contact person spoken to when a state trooper attempted to obtain sexual services for money. Appellant, in a consolidated trial, was convicted of four counts of promoting prostitution, and single counts of resisting arrest and criminal conspiracy. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's convictions. The court held that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 because the statute was neutral in its classification and the method of punishing the prostitute and the promoter as the providers, to a greater extent than the client who purchased such services was rationally related to the legitimate purpose of eliminating prostitution. The court held that the activity by the state trooper did not violate appellant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV because appellant did not display a reasonable expectation that he would have retained as private the information obtained by police. The court held that consolidation was proper because evidence of one crime would have been admissible in a separate trial for the other.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for promoting prostitution, resisting arrest, and criminal conspiracy because punishment under the statute was rationally related to the purpose it was intended for, consolidation was proper because proof of one crime tended to prove another, and appellant had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the information obtained by the police.

 

602 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Nay


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


281 Pa. Super. 226; 421 A.2d 1231; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3122


June 19, 1979, Argued  
September 19, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 2606 October Term, 1978, Appeal from an Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, Nos. 1379, 80 July Term, 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a pre-trial order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which failed to quash an information charging homicide by vehicle appellant claimed was double jeopardy barred following his acquittal for involuntary manslaughter in municipal court.


OVERVIEW: A municipal court judge acquitted appellant of involuntary manslaughter but convicted him of recklessly endangering another person (REAP) and homicide by vehicle following a two-car accident in which appellant's passenger died. Appellant filed notice of appeal for trial de novo in the court of common pleas and then, based on double jeopardy, filed a motion to quash the information that charged him with REAP and homicide by vehicle, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that double jeopardy did not bar trial de novo because crime of which appellant was acquitted required higher level mens rea or scienter, i.e., recklessness, which did not mean that the lower level mens rea of culpable negligence required to establish homicide by vehicle could not be established or that it was foreclosed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the refusal to quash and remanded the case for trial because the municipal court's failure to find recklessness did not foreclose a finding that appellant negligently caused the death, which was a lower level of intent or scienter.

 

603 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Atkins v. Singleton


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


282 Pa. Super. 390; 422 A.2d 1347; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3046


March 11, 1980, Argued  
September 5, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied December 31, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 515 October Term 1979, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Sect. at No. 0395 May Term 1977.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Pennsylvania, which convicted him of having neglected to support his minor child in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4323, and denied his motion to quash on the basis that the claim was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: A criminal complaint alleged that appellant father had not paid support for more than two years. Appellant denied paternity of the child and alleged the complaint was barred by the statute of limitations. The complaint was amended and alleged that appellant's last contribution was made within the limitations period. Appellant was convicted of having neglected to support his minor child. The court reversed and held that evidence of a single contribution was sufficient to show contribution to support, but the evidence was required show that it was made in circumstances that inferred that the father recognized the child as his own. Proof of either would have extended the period of limitations. If the evidence of the circumstances that surrounded a voluntary contribution were insufficient to have found that the contribution amounted to an acknowledgment of paternity, it would not have extended the period of limitations. There was no basis for an inference that appellant's purchase of lunch less than two years prior was either regarded by the mother or was intended by appellant as a renewal of contribution or an acknowledgement of paternity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held proof of a single contribution to the child's support without an acknowledgement of paternity was insufficient to extend the period of limitations. The claim was barred by the statute of limitations.

 

604 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Danko


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


281 Pa. Super. 97; 421 A.2d 1165; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3050


December 4, 1979, Argued  
September 5, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1058 October Term 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Criminal Div., at No. 2878-1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order by the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which convicted appellant of criminal solicitation under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 902, and prostitution under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902(a)(1). Appellant contended that § 5902 was unconstitutional, the evidence was insufficient, and that the lower court erred in not finding entrapment under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 313, as a matter of law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was called to a hotel room by an undercover police officer from a newspaper advertisement for an out-call massage service. Appellant took the money for the massage and after the massage the officer asked it there was anything else to the massage. Appellant quoted the officer prices for intercourse and the officer paid appellant. Appellant removed her clothes in preparation for the sex act. After appellant received the money and put it into her purse the officer placed her under arrest. Appellant was tried and convicted of criminal solicitation under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 902, and prostitution under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902(a)(1). On appeal, the court affirmed and held that appellant failed to raise any specific constitutional challenge to the statute at trial and therefore waived the constitutional arguments. The court further held that the sex act did not have to occur for the evidence to be sufficient to prove that appellant was engaged in sexual activity as a business. The court further held there was no entrapment under 18 Pa Cons. Stat. § 313, because the officer's behavior was not such as would have induced an innocent person to act as a prostitute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for criminal solicitation and prostitution because appellant waived any constitutional challenges, and the officer's behavior was not such as would have induced an innocent person to act as a prostitute. The court also held that the sex act did not have to occur for the evidence to be sufficient for the crimes.

 

605 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Coyle


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


280 Pa. Super. 268; 421 A.2d 716; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3038


December 6, 1979, Submitted  
August 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 548 October Term 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division, at No. 5148-78 - Dated March 8, 1979


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania) for violating 25 P.S. § 3234(a) in connection with his campaign for election to the Pennsylvania house of representatives.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant election candidate's conviction for running a campaign advertisement so close to an election, and without giving his opponent notice, so as to deny his opponent the opportunity to reply, in violation of 25 P.S. § 3234(a). The court found that appellant personally presented the political advertisement involved to a newspaper so close to the election that there was not time for his opponent to reply and that appellant did not give notice of the advertisement to his opponent in the election or to the election board as required by § 3234(a). The court held that the evidence was sufficient to prove that appellant placed the advertisement and that the advertisement clearly referred to his opponent. The court found that § 3234(a) was not overly broad and did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV or the equal protection clause in the Pennsylvania constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction under 25 P.S. § 3234(a) for running a campaign advertisement without giving his opponent sufficient notice to allow him to run a reply advertisement because the evidence was sufficient to establish that appellant had placed the advertisement and the advertisement clearly referred to the candidate running against appellant.

 

606 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Duncan


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


279 Pa. Super. 395; 421 A.2d 257; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2821


November 13, 1979, Argued  
July 11, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 255 APRIL TERM, 1979, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence imposed February 16, 1979 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Allegheny County at No. 7803989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence imposed by the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), following his conviction of statutory rape, indecent assault, indecent exposure and corruption of minors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on charges of statutory rape, indecent assault, indecent exposure and corruption of minors. Defendant argued that he was denied procedural due process when the trial court erred in denying the admission of testimony as to the minor victim's past sexual conduct with a third person. Defendant had allegedly reported such conduct to the victim's mother and maintained that the evidence was relevant and admissible for the limited purpose of showing that the victim's bias caused her to fabricate the charges against him. The court held that in enacting the rape shield law, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3104, the legislature intended that evidence of a victim's past sexual conduct with third persons was not admissible for any purpose. The court held that the trial court did not err in disallowing the testimony. The court questioned the constitutionality of the statute, noting problems it created in the face of the accused's right to confrontation, but added that the constitutionality of the law was not raised and it could not raise the issue sua sponte. The court affirmed the judgment of sentence, but recognized the constitutional difficulties that the law presented.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence because the rape shield law required that that evidence of a victim's past sexual conduct with third persons not be admitted for any purpose so the trial court did not err in disallowing the testimony.

 

607 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Wilkinson


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


278 Pa. Super. 490; 420 A.2d 647; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2762


March 21, 1979, Argued  
June 20, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1868 October Term 1978, Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Criminal Div., No. 805 May Sessions 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth appealed the order in the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which quashed the preliminary hearing transcript holding defendant for trial for homicide by vehicle under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3732.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's car crossed the median and crashed into two cars. She was arrested and charged with driving under the influence, and consented to a blood alcohol test. The complaint was dismissed. A second complaint was filed alleging the same facts and charging defendant with driving under the influence as well as homicide by vehicle under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3732 (1977). At the second preliminary hearing the trial judge ruled that the blood test was inadmissible and dismissed the driving under the influence charge. Defendant filed a motion to quash the preliminary hearing transcript, on the basis that she could not be held on the remaining charge as the commonwealth had failed to prove she otherwise violated a provision of the motor vehicle code. The motion was granted, and the commonwealth appealed. The court reversed the order and held that the commonwealth did not need to bring a separate charge for the violation of a motor code provision that resulted in death in a homicide by vehicle charge. The court held that defendant was on notice of the traffic law she violated, driving in the wrong lane, which caused death because the underlying accident was referenced in the charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order to quash because there was a supporting charge of defendant's violation of a traffic law which caused the fatal accident contained in the reference to the underlying accident where her car had been driven in the wrong lane immediately before the accident.

 

608 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Gurnick v. Government Employees Ins. Co.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


278 Pa. Super. 437; 420 A.2d 620; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2685


December 6, 1979, Argued  
June 13, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1247 October Term, 1979, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadephia County, Trial Division-Law, No. 5450 September Term, 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) dismissing appellant's complaint for punitive damages under the Pennsylvania No-Fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act, 40 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1009 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appeal from an order of the lower court dismissing appellant's claim for punitive damages under Pennsylvania's No-Fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act (Act), 40 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1009 et seq., for willful refusal to pay benefits. The reviewing court elected to grant relief on the interlocutory order under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 704, although the trial court had not certified the appeal because the quick resolution of the issue was of great importance. The reviewing court affirmed, holding that the remedies provided under the Act were exclusive, and allowing punitive damages would be an inappropriate exercise of legislative power. Furthermore, under the Statutory Construction Act of 1972, 1 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1921(b), when the words of a statute were clear and free from all ambiguity, the letter of the statute was not to be disregarded under the pretext of pursuing its spirit.


OUTCOME: Affirmed decision because, when the words of a statute were clear and free from all ambiguity, the letter of the statute was not to be disregarded under the pretext of pursuing its spirit, and the exclusive remedies under the Pennsylvania No-Fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act did not include punitive damages.

 

609 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Smith


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


280 Pa. Super. 222; 421 A.2d 693; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2148


November 16, 1979, Submitted  
March 14, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 412 April Term, 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, Criminal Division, No. 274 of 1977.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of incest and rape of his 12-year-old daughter. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in barring spectators from the courtroom when the victim testified, and that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict because his own testimony contradicted the victim's account.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his rape conviction on the grounds that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict. Appellant also contended that the trial court erred in barring spectators from the courtroom when the victim testified, and in surrounding him with guards during the trial. A jury convicted appellant of incest and statutory rape of his 12-year-old daughter. The victim was 14 years old at the time of the trial. She testified that appellant had raped her. Appellant argued that the verdict was against the weight of the evidence because his own testimony contradicted the victim's account, and that her testimony was unreliable because she was only 12 at the time and waited 5 days to report the rape. The appellate court held that the victim's slight delay in reporting the incident only raised issues of credibility for the jurors to resolve. The appellate court, however, vacated the conviction because the record failed to reveal whether the lower court actually ordered the removal of spectators, and whether appellant objected to any such orders. The appellate court therefore remanded for a hearing to supplement the record on that issue.


OUTCOME: While holding that the issue of the victim's credibility was a jury issue, the court vacated the conviction because the appellate record did not reveal whether spectators were actually removed from the courtroom, whether appellant objected to such orders, and the length of time such orders were in effect. The court remanded for the lower court to supplement the record on that issue.

 

610 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Whitfield


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


275 Pa. Super. 530; 419 A.2d 27; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1967


October 25, 1979, Argued  
January 25, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 327 Special Transfer Docket, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia, Trial Division, Criminal Section, No. 354 February Term, 1971.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of murder in the second degree in a retrial that followed a proceeding in which he was convicted of aggravated robbery and conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of murder of the second degree, aggravated robbery, and conspiracy. The court affirmed those convictions on appeal, and concluded that the record included sufficient evidentiary findings to sustain appellant's conviction for murder. The court also found that the retrial of appellant on the murder charge after he was convicted of robbery was rational. Although appellant's murder sentence had to be concurrent with, and could not exceed, his robbery sentence, a second sentence could have influenced decisions as to whether he served his maximum sentence. The court further held that reducing the voir dire peremptory challenges between appellant's trials was not an invalid ex post facto application of the law because it did not make a previously noncriminal act an offense, aggravate a crime, increase an offense's penalty, or alter the evidence rules. The court also found that the reference to appellant's gang membership was appropriate because it did not establish that he committed criminal acts, the jury was told to not use it as evidence of guilt, and it was probative of the credibility of the prosecution's chief witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for murder of the second degree, aggravated robbery, and conspiracy. The court held that a murder retrial was valid even though appellant's murder sentence had to be concurrent with, and could not exceed, his robbery sentence because it could have influenced decisions about his maximum sentence, and that the reduction of his peremptory challenges did not amount to an ex post facto law.

 

611 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Barone


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


276 Pa. Super. 282; 419 A.2d 457; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1971


September 13, 1979, Argued  
January 25, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1805 October Term 1978, No. 1950 October Term 1978, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County of May 31, 1978 sustaining the demurrer to No. 3575 - 77.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which sustained appellee's demurrer to the charge of homicide by vehicle under Motor Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732 (1977). Appellee filed a cross-appeal that challenged the trial court's earlier order that dismissed her petitions attacking the constitutionality of § 3732.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with homicide by vehicle, Motor Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732 (1977). The trial court sustained appellee's demurrer. Appellant commonwealth sought review. The court held that § 3732 fixed accountability only for negligent vehicle or traffic violations, but did not impose strict criminal responsibility. Accordingly, the order that sustained appellee's demurrer was affirmed because the evidence was not sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellee's conduct amounted to a gross deviation from the standard of care that a reasonable person would have observed in her situation. Appellee also sought review of her pre-trial petitions that sought a declaration of the unconstitutionality of § 3732. The court held that appellee's unexcused failure to raise alternative constitutional theories in her original petition was a waiver of the alternative theories. The court addressed appellee's original constitutional challenge, that where a summary offense is an essential element of the charged indictable offense, an accused is absolutely entitled to a finding of guilty or not guilty on the summary offense.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order that sustained appellee's demurrer to the charge of homicide by vehicle was affirmed because the offense governed deaths that resulted from negligent violations of the rules of the road, and the evidence was not sufficient to go to the jury. Appellee's contention that the statute that established the offense was unconstitutional was without merit.

 

612 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Brightbill v. Rigo, Inc.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


274 Pa. Super. 315; 418 A.2d 424; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1893; 5 Media L. Rep. 2496


June 11, 1979, Argued  
January 11, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 2827 October Term, 1978, Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Lebanon County, Civil Action, at No. 2, 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an injunction issued by the Court of Common Pleas, Lebanon County (Pennsylvania), which enjoined appellant from selling or advertising assertedly obscene magazines and motion picture films. Appellants were a corporation that operated an adult book store, an alleged officer of the corporation, the manager, and assistant manager of the store.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Obscenity Statute, appellee district attorney filed a complaint in equity against appellants. Appellants were a corporation that operated an adult book store, an alleged officer of the corporation, the store's manager, and the assistant manager. By special findings, a jury determined that each of 15 magazines and five films admitted into evidence by appellee were obscene. The trial court filed a decree that enjoined appellants and their agents, servants, and employees from selling or advertising the magazines and films or any of like or similar kind. Appellants sought review. The court held that the injunction was a prior restraint because it endeavored to impose a final restraint upon publications and films not yet determined to be obscene in a judicial proceeding. Accordingly, it violated the United States Constitution and the Pennsylvania Constitution, and the court struck the language about items of like or similar kind. Also struck was the language that purported to enjoin persons or entities not named in the complaint. That language was surplusage and was at odds with the plain language of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5903(g).


OUTCOME: The trial court's order that enjoined appellants, a corporation that operated an adult book store, an alleged officer of the corporation, the manager, and the assistant manager of the store, from selling or advertising assertedly obscene magazines and motion picture films was modified because, as entered by the trial court, it was an unconstitutional prior restraint and was unlawfully issued against appellants' agents, servants, and employees.
