Brown v. Commonwealth, State Bd. of Pharmacy


No. 2891 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


129 Pa. Commw. 642; 566 A.2d 913; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 751


June 5, 1989, Argued  
November 27, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION FOR REVIEW (STATE BOARD OF PHARMACY).



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the order of the Board denying Petitioner a hearing on his petition for reinstatement is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pharmacist sought review of an order of respondent, the State Board of Pharmacy (Pennsylvania), denying a hearing on his petition for reinstatement of his license to practice pharmacy and giving notice that pursuant to the Pharmacy Act, 63 P.S. §§ 390-1 to 390-13, petitioner could not apply again for reinstatement for 10 years. Petitioner's license was automatically suspended following his conviction for five felonies.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pharmacist's license to practice pharmacy was suspended by respondent, the State Board of Pharmacy, following petitioner's conviction for five felonies under the Controlled Substance, Drug, Device and Cosmetic Act (drug act), 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 780-101 to 780-144. The Pharmacy Act, 63 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 390-1 to 390-13 provided for the automatic suspension of a license following a licensee's conviction under the drug act. Several days after respondent issued its notice of suspension, the general assembly amended The Pharmacy Act by adding § 5(d), which provided that any person whose license was suspended because of a felony conviction under the drug act could apply for reinstatement after at least 10 years elapsed from the date of conviction. When petitioner filed for reinstatement of his license and requested a hearing, respondent denied the petition relying upon § 5(d). In reversing the order of the board, the court ruled that the retroactive application of § 5(d) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of respondent, the State Board of Pharmacy, which denied petitioner pharmacist a hearing on his petition for reinstatement of his right to practice pharmacy. The court ruled that insofar as the Pharmacy Act impaired petitioner's right to petition for revival or reinstatement of his license, the retroactive application of the statute was unconstitutional.

White v. Commonwealth, State Employes' Retirement System


No. 2096 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


129 Pa. Commw. 335; 565 A.2d 839; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 680


June 7, 1989, Argued  
October 31, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION FOR REVIEW, (STATE EMPLOYES' RETIREMENT BOARD).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of an order of respondent State Employees' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania), which denied petitioner's application for retirement benefits. Respondent contended that, with the exception of petitioner's own contributions to the retirement system and the statutory interest on those contributions, petitioner was precluded from receiving his retirement benefits by Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b).


OVERVIEW: Respondent state employees' retirement board denied petitioner employee's application for retirement benefits. Respondent stated that, with the exception of petitioner's own contributions to the retirement system and the statutory interest on those contributions, petitioner was precluded from receiving his retirement benefits by Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b). The board held as it did because petitioner had been removed from judicial office. The court vacated respondent's order and remanded the case. The court stated that a remand was necessary to determine when petitioner, who had also served a legislative term, became a member of the retirement system. The court stated that only after the fact of when petitioner became a member of the system was determined could the constitutional issues be addressed. The court held that a remand was necessary for a determination of whether petitioner was in fact a member of the retirement system in the 1950s and, if he was, whether he withdrew his benefits, terminated his membership, and subjected himself to legislation enacted after he joined the system.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of respondent state employees' retirement board, which denied petitioner employee's application for retirement benefits and remanded the case. The court held that a remand was necessary to determine whether petitioner was a member of the retirement system in the 1950s and whether he withdrew his benefits, terminated his membership, and subjected himself to legislation enacted after he joined the system.

King v. Commonwealth, State Employes' Retirement Bd.


No. 2109 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


129 Pa. Commw. 444; 566 A.2d 323; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 681


June 7, 1989, Argued  
October 31, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal Granted March 28, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from PETITION FOR REVIEW.



DISPOSITION: Based upon the foregoing opinion, the order of the Board in the above-captioned matter is hereby affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judge appealed an order of respondent State Employes' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania), which denied petitioner's application for retirement benefits while allowing petitioner to withdraw his own contributions and the interest thereon.


OVERVIEW: Because of improper conduct, the Pennsylvania Supreme Court directed that petitioner judge be removed from judicial office, that petitioner's salary cease, and that he be thereafter ineligible to hold judicial office. Petitioner filed an application with the State Employes' Retirement Board, seeking a reduced retirement allowance for life. Respondent, without giving petitioner notice or the opportunity to be heard, denied the application and asserted that with the exception of petitioner's own contributions to the system and the statutory interest on those contributions, he was precluded from receiving his retirement benefits, pursuant to Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b). Petitioner appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed respondent's decision and held that the question of whether petitioner was entitled to retirement benefits was properly presented to respondent, that application of § 16(b) to petitioner did not impair his statutory contractual rights, that a hearing was not constitutionally required, and that the voters did not act irrationally when they placed judges in a separate classification from other state employees in § 16(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent State Employes' Retirement Board's denial of petitioner judge's application for retirement benefits because, pursuant to the state constitution, petitioner was only entitled to withdraw his contributions and interest and, because he was removed from office for misconduct, he was not precluded from receiving anything more.

Provident Nat'l Bank v. Montgomery County Bd. of Assessment Appeals


Nos. 3024 C.D. 1988, 3025 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


129 Pa. Commw. 281; 565 A.2d 508; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 672


September 12, 1989, Argued  
October 23, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Montgomery County Common Pleas Court, Honorable Horace A. Davenport, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate executors sought review of decisions by the Montgomery County Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which held that appellants' interests in certain limited partnerships were subject to the County Personal Property Tax Act (Act), 72 P.S. § 4821. Appellants, in two consolidated appeals, contended that the partnership interests were not subject to the tax because they were not personal property within the meaning of the Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant estate executors, in two separate cases that were consolidated for appeal, disputed contention of appellee assessment board that appellants' interest in certain limited partnerships was personal property under section 1 of the County Personal Property Tax Act (Act), 72 P.S. § 4821. Appellee had asserted and the trial court held that the limited partnership interests were personal property. On appeal, the court reversed because the Act did not specifically name interests in limited partnerships as taxable property. The court reviewed analogous cases and statutes and held that principles of statutory construction, including 1 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1928, required a strict reading of the subject statute in favor of appellants, as taxpayers. The court specifically held that the limited partnership interests were not "moneys loaned or invested in other states", "moneyed capital owing to individual citizens", or "shares of stock in a limited partnership," within the meaning of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court in favor of appellee assessment board in two personal property tax cases that were consolidated on appeal because appellants' interests in limited partnerships were not "personal property" within the meaning of the challenged tax law. The court held that tax statutes had to be strictly construed and the failure to list the partnership interests meant they were non taxable.

County of Centre, Bd. of Assessment Appeals v. Pennsylvania State University


No. 2656 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


129 Pa. Commw. 184; 565 A.2d 187; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 657


Argued: April 5, 1989  
October 12, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Granted August 13, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Centre County; Honorable David E. Grine, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County (Pennsylvania), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee university in an action to collect real estate taxes on a bank situated on appellee's campus because the doctrines of res judicata and collateral estoppel barred such an action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant board sought to assess and collect real estate taxes on property owned by a bank which was situated on the campus of appellee university. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellee on the basis of res judicata and collateral estoppel because a previous lawsuit had determined that appellee was an agent of the commonwealth and could not be taxed by appellant. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that res judicata barred the action and it did not examine the issue of collateral estoppel. The court found that appellee was found to have been an agent of the commonwealth in a 1939 case and that nothing had happened to change that outcome. The court held that the trial court had properly determined the matter and that it was consistent with Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 2(a)(iii).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee university because res judicata barred the imposition of real estate taxes on appellee's property and the trial court had properly determined the issue.

Blevins v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


No. 2897 C. D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


128 Pa. Commw. 533; 563 A.2d 1301; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 618


June 9, 1989, Argued  
September 14, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION FOR REVIEW, (ENVIRONMENTAL HEARING BOARD).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner sought review of an order from the Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), which denied petitioner's request to appeal nunc pro tunc an action by respondent, Department of Environmental Resources, that modified a permit held by an operator of the solid waste landfill facility.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the order from the Environmental Hearing Board that denied petitioner landowner's petition to appeal nunc pro tunc an order from respondent, Department of Environmental Resources, because respondent was under no obligation to notify petitioner that a permit amendment was requested or issued. The court found that respondent, Department of Environmental Resources, was authorized pursuant to the Solid Waste Management Act, 35 P.S. §§ 6018.101 - 6018.1003, to issue, modify and condition the permit to the solid waste landfill facility as an effective means of implementing and enforcing the statute. The court concluded that the denial of petitioner's appeal nunc pro tunc did not result in a breach of due process because petitioner was not entitled to written notice of the permit amendment since respondent's authority over the permit was not statutorily limited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Environmental Hearing Board's order that denied petitioner landowner's appeal nunc pro tunc because it found that respondent, Department of Environmental Resources, was under no statutory obligation to notify petitioner that a permit amendment had been requested or issued.

OVERVIEW: Petitioner police officers' association and trustees brought an action against respondent borough and commonwealth challenging the constitutionality of the Financially Distressed Municipalities Act (Act 47), 53 Pa. Commonwealth by Preate v. Watson & Hughey Co.

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania

June 9, 1989, Argued

Stat. Ann. §§ 201-1 to 201-9.2, and the Charitable Organization Reform Act, 10 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 161.1-161.19.

Ann. §§ 201-1 to 201-9.2, and the Charitable Organization Reform Act, 10 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 161.1-161.19. Defendants brought preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer. OUTCOME: The court sustained in part and overruled in part defendant charitable organizations' demurrer to the Commonwealth's action for violations of the unfair trade practices and consumer protection law, holding that the unfair trade practices and consumer law was applicable to sweepstakes solicitations by defendants.

Startzel v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Educ.


No. 2051 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


128 Pa. Commw. 110; 562 A.2d 1005; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 566


April 7, 1989, Argued  
August 11, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 6, 1989. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION FOR REVIEW.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the order of the Department is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teacher sought review of an order from respondent Department of Education (Pennsylvania), which revoked petitioner's permanent teaching certificate pursuant to 24 P.S. § 1225(j) on the basis of petitioner's guilty plea to mail fraud.


OVERVIEW: After petitioner teacher was convicted of mail fraud, respondent Department of Education revoked petitioner's permanent teaching certificate pursuant to 24 P.S. § 1225(j). Petitioner sought review, and the court affirmed. The court found that petitioner's certificate had been properly revoked under § 1225(j) because in committing mail fraud, petitioner had committed a crime of moral turpitude. Moreover, the court found that § 1225(j) had not required a discretionary determination of petitioner's fitness during the decertification stage instead of at the reinstatement stage. Finally, the court found that the immediate decertification under § 1225(j) had not violated petitioner's constitutionally guaranteed right to pursue a teaching career because § 1225(j)'s decertification/reinstatement process was a rational way to protect children and further the state's legitimate interest in ensuring that state-certified educators stayed fit to work closely with students.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order revoking petitioner teacher's teaching certificate on the basis of petitioner's guilty plea to mail fraud because mail fraud had been a crime of moral turpitude, a discretionary determination of petitioner's fitness had not been required at the decertification stage as opposed to the reinstatement stage, and the requirement of immediate decertification had not violated petitioner's right to pursue a teaching career.

 

703 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Satinoff v. Commonwealth


No. 130 C.D. 1989


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


128 Pa. Commw. 93; 562 A.2d 996; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 556


May 1, 1989, Argued  
August 7, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Fayette County; Honorable Richard D. Cicchetti, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Common Pleas Court, Fayette County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced appellant to pay fines and court costs for the violation of an ordinance requiring a person engaged in peddling to obtain a $ 20 license. Appellant was found guilty of violating the ordinance after appellant, who had not obtained a license, attempted to distribute a political newspaper for a donation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant distributed a social worker's party newspaper for a donation. Thereafter, appellant was arrested for violating an ordinance that required a person engaged in peddling to apply for a license, the fee for which was $ 20 per day. After appellant was sentenced to pay fines and court costs for violating the ordinance, appellant sought review, and the court reversed. The court found that appellant's conduct had not been one of commercial nature but had instead been political activity protected by U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV. The court found that appellant's activity had been political in nature because appellant's primary purpose had been to discuss political ideas, appellant had offered older copies of the newspaper for free, and appellant's small monetary gain had not been analogous to the commercial activity of door-to-door selling of subscriptions to national periodicals, newspapers, and magazines. Finally, the court found that the licensing fee had rendered the ordinance unconstitutional pursuant to amends. I, XIV and Pa. Const. art. I, § 7 because the fee had made it impossible to disseminate political ideas and speech through door-to-door solicitation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment sentencing appellant to pay fines and court costs for violation of an ordinance requiring a peddler to obtain a license because appellant's dissemination of political newspapers was not commercial activity but instead, was political activity protected by the First and Fourteenth Amendments and because the licensing fee unconstitutionally restricted appellant's ability to disseminate political ideas.

 

704 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Paustian v. Pa. Convention Ctr. Auth.


No. 2328 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


127 Pa. Commw. 470; 561 A.2d 1337; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 547


March 8, 1989, Argued  
August 4, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Denied June 4, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Philadelphia County; Honorable Lawrence Pratti, Honorable Albert W. Sheppard, Jr., Honorable Abraham J. Gafni, Judges.
Paustian v. Pennsylvania Convention Center Authority, 3 Pa. D. & C.4th 16, 1988 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 15 (1988)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonresident hotel guests challenged the decision of the Common Pleas Court, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted a motion for judgment on the pleadings of appellees, governmental entities.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nonresident hotel guests sought a declaratory judgment that the hotel room rental tax and its enabling legislation were unconstitutional. They claimed that pending the start-up of the convention center operation, they would be taxed to support the planning and construction of the center without realizing any benefit. The trial court granted the motion for judgment on the pleadings of appellee governmental entities and the court affirmed. It found that the trial court properly characterized the additional tax burden as minimal when compared to the prospective good to be achieved by both residents and visitors alike, and found that the constitutional issues presented were primarily legal in nature and properly disposed of in this procedural posture. The court also found that although appellants may not receive tangible benefit at present, it rejected the implication that the convention center project could not be funded through the imposition of a tax before the project's completion and operation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment on the pleadings because the trial court properly characterized the additional tax burden as minimal and found that the constitutional issues were primarily legal in nature.

 

705 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Reading v. Feltman


Nos. 1115 C.D. 1988, 1131 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


127 Pa. Commw. 618; 562 A.2d 926; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 525


April 7, 1989, Argued  
July 26, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Berks County; Honorable Albert A. Stallone, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city, mayor, and police pension board, sought review of an order of the Common Pleas Court of Berks County (Pennsylvania), which denied their motion for post-trial relief after awarding partial and full pension benefits, interest, counsel fees, and costs to appellees, survivors of police officers, in a class action in mandamus.


OVERVIEW: In a class action in mandamus, the trial court granted partial and full pension benefits, interest, counsel fees, and costs, to appellees, survivors of police officers, and also denied the motion of appellants, city, mayor, and police pension board, for post-trial relief. On appeal, the court affirmed the order awarding pension benefits with interest to appellees, holding that the plain language of appellant city's ordinance provided that appellees, who were survivors of members who died after the effective date of the ordinance were entitled to that member's pension and that the payment of interest was proper under § 8303 of the Judicial Code (Code), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8303, because appellants failed or refused without lawful justification to perform a duty required by law, making them liable in damages to appellees. However, the court reversed the award of counsel fees and costs to appellees, holding that the common fund and common benefit doctrines did not apply to allow such relief, because there was no common fund within the jurisdiction of the trial court, pursuant § 2503(8) of the Code, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2503(8).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of pension benefits with interest to appellees, survivors if police officers against appellants, city, mayor, and police pension board, holding that appellant city's ordinance provided that appellees were entitled to the member's pension and that the payment of interest was proper. The court reversed the award of counsel fees and costs, holding that there was no common fund within the trial court's jurisdiction.

All Purpose Vending, Inc. v. Philadelphia


Nos. 8 T. D. 1987, 75 C. D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


127 Pa. Commw. 415; 561 A.2d 1309; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 507


December 14, 1988, Argued  
July 20, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied September 27, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vending machine owners sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted summary judgment to appellees, city, mayor, city council, and police commissioner, in appellants' complaint in equity alleging that Phila., Pa. Code §§ 19-902 to -903, as applied to them, imposed a tax on their free exercise of rights guaranteed by U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellant vending machine owners filed a complaint in equity against appellees, city, mayor, city council, and police commissioner, alleging that Phila., Pa. Code §§ 19-902 to -903, as applied to them, imposed a tax on their free exercise of rights guaranteed by U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment; the trial court granted summary judgment to appellees. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellees on the grounds that the trial court had properly declined to exercise equity jurisdiction because appellants had failed to pursue adequate and available administrative remedies. It rejected appellants' argument that the administrative process acted as a prior restraint on their freedom of speech and was therefore inadequate because appellant city had no discretion to refuse to issue registration tags to appellants once the tax was paid. The court concluded that the case did not fall within the constitutional attack exception to the exhaustion of administrative remedies doctrine because in order to fall within the exception a party had to attack the constitutionality of the statute as a whole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellees, city, mayor, city council, and police commissioner, in appellant vending machine owners' action in equity alleging that appellees' ordinance, as applied to them, imposed a tax on their free exercise of rights. It found that the trial court properly declined to exercise equity jurisdiction because appellants had failed to exhaust adequate administrative remedies.

In re Incorporation of New Morgan


Nos. 1343 C.D. 1988, 1344 C.D. 1988, 1345 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


127 Pa. Commw. 519; 562 A.2d 402; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 494


March 7, 1989, Argued  
July 17, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Granted June 5, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Berks County Common Pleas Court, Honorable Thomas J. Eshelman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, townships and intervenor individuals, sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania), granting the petition of appellee applicant to incorporate a new borough. The trial court determined that the requirements of the Borough Code, Act of February 1, 1966, Pub. L. (1965) 1656, as amended, 53 P.S. §§ 45101-4850, had been met.


OVERVIEW: Appellee applicant filed a petition for incorporation as a borough a tract of land that it owned and which it sought to develop. Appellants, townships and intervenor individuals, opposed the petition. Pursuant to the Borough Code (code), Act of February 1, 1966, Pub. L. (1965) 1656, as amended, 53 P.S. §§ 45101-48501, the trial court established a borough advisory committee, which issued a report in favor of incorporation. The trial court adopted and incorporated the report and ordered a referendum vote of the residents of the proposed borough. Nine residents voted in favor of incorporation, with one opposed. The trial court issued a final decision granting the petition for incorporation. The court affirmed, holding that code provisions which restricted voting to residents was not unconstitutional and did not undercut the people's right to self-determination. The court held that appellee met its burden of showing that the proposed borough was a harmonious whole with common interests and problems, which could be properly served by borough government, and that the requirements for incorporation had been met.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, granting appellee applicant's petition to incorporate a tract of land as a borough, over the objections of appellant townships and intervenor individuals. The court held that the procedures for incorporation were not unconstitutional and that appellee met its burden of showing that the proposed area could be properly served by borough government.

Lyness v. Commonwealth, State Bd. of Medicine


No. 961 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


127 Pa. Commw. 225; 561 A.2d 362; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 460


March 8, 1989, Argued  
June 29, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION FOR REVIEW, (STATE BOARD OF MEDICINE).



DISPOSITION: For the reasons stated above we vacate the decision of the Board and remand this matter to the Board for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner physician sought review of a decision from respondent State Board of Medicine (Pennsylvania), which found that petitioner committed acts constituting immoral and unprofessional conduct in violation of 63 P.S. § 421.15(a)(8) of the Medical Practice Act of 1974, and revoked his license to practice medicine.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner physician was accused of committing acts constituting immoral and unprofessional conduct in violation of 63 P.S. § 421.15(a)(8) of the Medical Practice Act of 1974, and was brought before a hearing examiner for respondent State Board of Medicine (Board). The hearing examiner determined that petitioner was guilty of the acts charged, his license to practice medicine was to be suspended for five years, and that he was to submit to the care, counseling or treatment of a physician or physicians designated by the Board. The prosecuting attorney requested the Board's review of this determination, asking for a harsher sentence. Petitioner requested that the Board hold an evidentiary hearing, and permit the filing of briefs and oral argument. The Board denied petitioner's request and granted that of the prosecutor, altering the punishment to revocation of his license. On appeal, the court vacated the decision, finding that petitioner's claim of laches was a bar the proceedings if petitioner proved that he was prejudiced by the undue delay of his victims in reporting the incidents to the board. The matter was remanded for the board to make factual determinations on laches.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision by respondent State Board of Medicine against petitioner physician, based only on the claim of laches. While denying petitioner's other claims of error, the court found that the doctrine of laches applied if petitioner showed prejudice by victim's delays in reporting incidents. The matter was remanded for the board to make factual determinations as to this alleged prejudice.

Helmerick Drive-It-Yourself v. Erie Mun. Airport Auth.


No. 2592 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


149 Pa. Commw. 1; 612 A.2d 562; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 842


May 1, 1989, Argued  
June 22, 1989, Decided  
June 22, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Publication Ordered August 3, 1992. As Amended August 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED From No. 35 Equity 1987. Common Pleas Court of Erie County



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County granting summary judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an off premises car rental business, challenged decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), which granted a motion for summary judgment in favor of appellee airport authority stating that appellee had authority to assess an annual permit fee against appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an off-premises car rental business, challenged the authority of appellee, airport authority, to issue citations to appellant for failure to pay a $ 100 yearly permit fee as required by the then-existing rules and regulations. Appellee then filed a motion for summary judgment contending that, based upon an amendment to it regulations, the annual permit fee assessed against all off-premises car rental businesses was 10% of gross revenues and that appellee could, pursuant to the Municipal Authorities Act of 1945 (the Act), 53 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 301-401, required appellant to pay this permit fee. The lower court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. Appellant challenged the lower court's decision. The court affirmed, holding that the Act provided municipalities with wide discretion in determining how to conduct their business and that the permit fee was a power conveyed to it under the Act. The court further held that appellee was not indirectly competing with appellant's business; rather, appellee was attempting to recoup expenses it incurred in operating the airport and the permit fee was a cost which appellant must expend to have done business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision which granted the motion for summary judgment of appellee, airport authority, holding that appellee had statutory power to collect an annual permit fee from appellant, off-premises car rental business, and that assessment of 10% of its gross receipts as a permit fee was reasonable.

 

710 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania Power Co. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


No. 1317 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


127 Pa. Commw. 97; 561 A.2d 43; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 434


March 8, 1989, Argued  
June 16, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended June 30, 1989. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted November 15, 1989.
Appeal granted by Pa. Power Co. v. Pa. PUC, 524 Pa. 601, 568 A.2d 1250, 1989 Pa. LEXIS 480 (1989)
Affirmed by Pennsylvania Power Co. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com., 526 Pa. 453, 587 A.2d 312, 1991 Pa. LEXIS 63 (1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION FOR REVIEW (PENNSYLVANIA PUBLIC UTILITY COMMISSION).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner public utility sought review of the order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, which refused to allow petitioner to include in its rates certain expenses it had incurred as a result of a sale and buyback agreement with another utility.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner public utility filed an interim energy cost rate with the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission (PUC) to recover costs associated with a sale and buyback agreement with another utility. After concluding that it was unreasonable and unlawful to allow petitioner to recover its costs, an ALJ disallowed the costs associated with the buyback. The PUC upheld the decision of the ALJ. The court affirmed the decision of the PUC, holding that the PUC's conclusion as to the unreasonableness of petitioner's expenses was legally correct, and that it was supported by substantial evidence in the record. The court held that the PUC was not preempted from disallowing expenses incurred as a result of a purchase at a rate approved by the Federal Energy Regulatory Commission (FERC), as petitioner voluntarily entered into the sale and buyback agreement, and the FERC did not mandate the purchase or otherwise limit petitioner's option for purchasing power. The court held that the PUC's decision was simply a state determination that petitioner's agreement to purchase power at the FERC-approved rate was unreasonably excessive when lower cost power was readily available elsewhere.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission's (PUC) decision to disallow petitioner public utility's expenses incurred as a result of the sale and buyback agreement with another utility. The court found that the PUC correctly concluded that petitioner's expenses were unreasonably excessive in light of the fact that lower cost power was readily available.

Ernest Sunday Chrysler Plymouth, Inc. v. Commonwealth, DOT


No. 1877 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


126 Pa. Commw. 124; 558 A.2d 921; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 340


December 20, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
May 17, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 30, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Common Pleas Court, Cumberland County, Honorable Edgar B. Bayley, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dealership sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order of appellee Department of Transportation (Pennsylvania) suspending appellant's dealer registration plates and its authorization to issue temporary registration plates for violations of § 1103(d) of the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1103(d).


OVERVIEW: Appellee Department of Transportation (Pennsylvania) found that appellant had violated § 1103(d) of the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1103(d). A hearing was held, and appellee suspended appellant's dealer registration plates and its authorization to issue temporary registration plates. After a de novo hearing, the trial court affirmed the decision. Appellant argued that it was denied due process and that appellee improperly considered evidence of appellant's prior violations. The court affirmed the order, holding that appellant was not denied due process, as 67 Pa. Code §§ 43.11 and 53.9 did not require that a hearing be held prior to the issuance of a warning. Moreover, appellee did not err in failing to inform appellant of his right to counsel, as the Administrative Agency Law, 2 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 501-508, did not apply to hearings held pursuant to §§ 43.11 or 53.9. Appellee did not err in considering appellant's prior violations, as a prior violation was properly considered because it occurred one year prior to the current warning. The trial court did not err in failing to impose a less severe penalty, as the trial court and appellee both found a § 1103(d) violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, holding that appellee Department of Transportation (Pennsylvania) did not err in failing to hold a hearing before issuing a warning to appellant dealership for violations of the Vehicle Code, as regulations did not require that a hearing be afforded in such circumstances. Trial court did not err in refusing to impose a lesser penalty, as both appellee and the trial court found violations.

Millersville Borough v. Fruitman


No. 2208 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


125 Pa. Commw. 660; 557 A.2d 1176; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 299


April 4, 1989, Argued  
May 9, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, in the case of Millersville Borough v. Martin Fruitman and Sandra Fruitman, No. 2769 of 1987.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a ruling from the Lancaster County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which dismissed an action in equity brought by appellant, seeking to restrain appellees from continuing to violate appellant's Housing Maintenance and Occupancy Code.


OVERVIEW: Appellees owned a house, which was rented without a license to tenants in 1987 and 1988. Appellant informed appellees that the rental of their property without obtaining a license constituted a violation of the Housing Maintenance and Occupancy Code (Housing Code). Pursuant to 53 P.S. § 108.4(1), appellant sought to restrain appellees from continuing to violate its Housing Code by submitting to an inspection and obtaining a license for a leased residential property owned by appellees. Subsequently, the court of common pleas dismissed appellant's action in equity because such action was inappropriate. The court of common pleas found that the summary of criminal proceedings permitted by the Housing Code were available to appellant as a remedy to correct the problem of appellees' noncompliance. On appeal, the court vacated the order and remanded the matter for further proceedings. The court found that appellant's Housing Code called for the availability of an action in equity in order to enforce housing codes. Accordingly, appellant had a right to proceed in equity just as it had the right to proceed at law. Thus, the court of common pleas erred by dismissing appellant's action.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the court of common pleas' order dismissing appellant's action in equity. The court of common pleas erred in law by dismissing said action on the basis that appellant failed to avail itself of the summary criminal enforcement provision contained in the Housing Code.

Sameric Corp. v. City of Phila.


Nos. 1277 C.D. 1987, 1985 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


125 Pa. Commw. 520; 558 A.2d 155; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 308


December 13, 1988, Argued  
May 2, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended May 26, 1989. Appeal Granted April 11, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in the case of Sameric Corporation of Chestnut St., Inc. v. Philadelphia Historical Commission, No. 3955 April Term, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant theater owner challenged the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's challenged to respondent historical commission's decision designating the interior and exterior of appellant's theater as historic and which denied post-trial relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellee historical commission designated the interior and exterior of appellant theater owner's building as historic pursuant to Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 12-2007(5). Appellant challenged that designation. The trial court dismissed appellant's challenge and denied appellant's request for post-trial relief. On further appeal, the court affirmed the order dismissing the appeal and quashed the appeal filed from the denial of the request for post-trial relief. Substantial evidence supported appellee's designation of the building's exterior as historic. The court further held that, pursuant to Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 12-2007(2)(b) and § 12-2007(4), appellee had the authority to designate as historic the building's interior. The court finally concluded that appellee's designation of the interior of the building as historic was not an unconstitutional exercise of the state's police powers. Allowing appellee to designate as historic the interior of appellant's building was substantially related to the public good protected by Pa. Const. Art. I, § 27.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the appeal filed from the denial of appellant theater owner's request for post-trial relief and affirmed the dismissal of appellant's challenge to appellee historical commission's designation of the exterior and interior of appellant's theater as historic. Appellee had the authority to designate as historic both the exterior and the interior of appellant's theater.

Blackwell v. State Ethics Comm'n


No. 2222 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


125 Pa. Commw. 42; 556 A.2d 988; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 210


December 14, 1988, Argued  
April 7, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Honorable Lucien Blackwell, Member City Council of Philadelphia, Honorable David Cohen, Member City Council of Philadelphia, Honorable Francis Rafferty, Member City Council of Philadelphia v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Ethics Commission.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections of Commission overruled. Answer to be filed within fourteen days. Petitioners to serve petition for review on Attorney General within fourteen days.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State Ethics Commission (Pennsylvania) filed preliminary objections to a petition for review in the nature of an action for declaratory judgment, in which petitioners, three city councilmen, asked the court to enjoin respondent's investigation of them for alleged violations of the Public Officials Ethics Act, 65 P.S. §§ 401- 413, and to declare the investigation unlawful and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent State Ethics Commission initiated an investigation of petitioners, three city councilmen, to determine whether they had hired their spouses in violation of the Public Officials Ethics Act, 65 P.S. §§ 401- 413. Petitioners filed a petition for review in the nature of an action for declaratory judgment, to which respondent filed preliminary objections. The court overruled the preliminary objections, determining that relief under the Declaratory Judgments Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 7531- 7541, was appropriate. This was not a case where a statute called for specialized fact-finding or application of an agency's administrative expertise. Petitioners raised substantial constitutional questions and challenged respondent's authority to proceed with its investigation, questioning whether respondent's investigatory powers over petitioners collided with the home rule authority granted to the city by Pa. Const. art. IX, § 2. The challenge went to the heart of respondent's power. The court therefore directed respondents to file an answer to the petition, and directed petitioners to serve the petition on the Pennsylvania Attorney General pursuant to Pa. R. App. P. 1514(c).


OUTCOME: The court overruled the preliminary objections of respondent State Ethics Commission, and directed petitioners to serve their petition in the nature of declaratory judgment on the Pennsylvania Attorney General, and for respondents to file an answer to the petition, because declaratory judgment was properly invoked where petitioners' challenge questioned the scope of respondent's action pursuant to its statutory authority.

Pennsylvania Northwestern Distribs. v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 1520 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


124 Pa. Commw. 228; 555 A.2d 1368; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 143


February 6, 1989, Argued  
March 16, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in the case of PA Northwestern Distributors, Inc. v. The Zoning Hearing Board of The Township of Moon, No. S.A. 1218 of 1987.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bookstore owner sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed appellee township zoning hearing board's decision to uphold a zoning ordinance restricting the location of adult businesses, as applied to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee township zoning hearing board upheld a zoning ordinance which required adult businesses to locate certain distances away from residential districts, schools, and churches, and which contained an amortization clause allowing existing businesses 90 days to comply, as applied to appellant bookstore owner, who operated an adult business that violated the ordinance. The trial court affirmed, as did the court. The court found that appellee had a substantial and legitimate interest in enacting an ordinance regulating the location of adult establishments, and the ordinance allowed for reasonable alternatives for communication. The court found that appellant did not meet its burden of proving that there were no alternative locations, and appellant's argument that other locations were not as desirable was without merit, as U.S. Const. amend. I did not promise a desirable location. The court also upheld the amortization clause because appellant's inventory was mostly monthly publications, expenses incurred after the enactment were incurred at appellant's own risk, appellant could break its lease, and other expenses could be used at a different location.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's affirmance of appellee township zoning hearing board's decision to uphold the zoning ordinance as applied to appellant bookstore owner, because the ordinance did not completely restrict communication, the First Amendment did not guarantee a desirable location, and the amortization clause did not cause a hardship as applied to appellant.

Dodaro v. State Ethics Comm'n


No. 137 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


124 Pa. Commw. 163; 556 A.2d 8; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 139


May 25, 1988, Argued  
March 14, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Granted November 15, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the State Ethics Commission in the case of Frank Dodaro, Order No. 590-R, File No. 86-106-C, dated December 14, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a public official, sought review of an order of respondent Pennsylvania State Ethics Commission, which found that petitioner had used his public office to obtain a financial gain for a member of his family in violation of the State Ethics Act, 65 P.S. § 403(a). Petitioner claimed that no penalty could be imposed because there was no intent, that the penalty would result in unjust enrichment, and that § 403(a) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a public official, sought review of an order of respondent Pennsylvania State Ethics Commission. Respondent found that petitioner had violated the State Ethics Act, 65 P.S. § 403(a), by using his public office for a financial gain by a member of his family. Petitioner alleged that no penalty could be imposed where intent was lacking and that the monies would result in unjust enrichment. Further, he contended that § 403(a) was unconstitutional because it imposed criminal penalties for unknowing violations. The court held that a public officer was disqualified from voting in any matter in which he had a personal interest, as did petitioner, whose indirect financial interest presented the appearance of a conflict with the public trust, even if that was not his intent. The court ruled that, unless petitioner divested himself of the financial gain by returning the monies paid to his family member, a recommendation for prosecution could result. The court found that the constitutional challenge failed because petitioner had not been subjected to any criminal penalties and that the penalty provisions challenged were not applicable. The order of respondent was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that petitioner, a public official, violated the State Ethics Act by using his public office for a financial gain by a member of his family. The court held that a public officer was disqualified from voting in any matter in which he had a personal interest and an indirect financial interest that presented the appearance of a conflict with the public trust.

Pennsylvania Asso. of Rental Dealers v. Commonwealth


No. 1808 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


123 Pa. Commw. 533; 554 A.2d 998; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 105


December 14, 1988, Argued  
February 22, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended March 1, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Jurisdiction in the case of Pennsylvania Association of Rental Dealers v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Robert Casey.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's motion for summary judgment granted and respondents' motion for summary judgment denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner association filed an equitable action in the court's original jurisdiction seeking a declaratory judgment that the Installment Sales Act, 69 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§1101-2303 (1988), was unconstitutional. Petitioner, respondent state, and respondent governor filed motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner association filed suit in the court's original jurisdiction challenging the constitutionality of the Installment Sales Act, 69 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1101-2303 (1988). Petitioner argued that the act was enacted in a manner that violated Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 1, 2, 4 because the original subject matter of the bill was completely deleted through the legislative process. Petitioner, respondent state, and respondent governor filed motions for summary judgment. The court held that the case was justiciable even though Pa. Const. art. II, § 11 gave the legislature power to determine the rules of its proceedings because the limitations on legislative power contained in Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 2,4 were judicially enforceable. The court found that the statute violated §§ 2, 4 because amendments to the original bill were not germane to and wholly changed the general subject of the original bill, which dealt with payments of estimated taxes by farmers. The court granted petitioner's motion, denied respondents' motions for summary judgment, and declared the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Petitioner association's motion for summary judgment was granted, respondent state and respondent governor's motion for summary judgment was denied, and the Installment Sales Act was declared unconstitutional. Because amendments to the original bill were not germane to and wholly changed the original bill, which dealt with an entirely different subject matter, the manner in which the statute was enacted was unconstitutional.

 

719 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. Montgomery County Tax Claim Bureau


No. 1124 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


123 Pa. Commw. 371; 553 A.2d 1044; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 61


December 15, 1988, Argued  
February 7, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, in the case of Charles Thomas v. Montgomery County Tax Claim Bureau, A. O. Breinig, No. 85-13923.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which confirmed a tax sale of appellant's property by appellee tax claim bureau, denying appellant's exceptions to the sale on the basis that the posting provisions of 72 P.S. § 5860.602 were not complied with.


OVERVIEW: After failing to pay property taxes, appellant taxpayer's property was sold at tax sale by appellee tax claim bureau. Appellant filed exceptions to the sale, alleging that the posting provisions of 72 P.S. § 5860.602 were not complied with. The trial court held that such notice provisions were complied with and confirmed the sale. The court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court held that although appellee had the initial burden to show that the provisions of § 5860.602 were complied with, the prima facie presumption of the regularity of the acts of public officers, the testimony of the director of appellee as to the posting procedure of the sheriff's personnel, and the failure of appellant to put on any contradictory testimony all supported a finding that the posting was done according to statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that confirmed the tax sale of appellant taxpayer's property. The court held that the presumption of regularity of acts of public officers, the testimony of the director of appellee tax claim bureau, and the failure of appellant to put forth contradictory evidence allowed the trial court to find that the posting of the tax sale was done according to law.

Brough v. Heidelberg Township Bd. of Supervisors


No. 2380 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


123 Pa. Commw. 212; 554 A.2d 133; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 80


September 13, 1988, Argued  
January 30, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Pennsylvania, in the case of C. William Brough v. Heidelberg Township Board of Supervisors, York County, Pa., No. 87-SU-00019-08.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Heidelberg Township Board of Supervisors challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania), that reversed an order of appellant, which denied the application for subdivision of appellee individual for failure to meet the requirements of § 509(b) of the Heidelberg Township Subdivision and Land Development Ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellee individual acquired 58 acres of land in two township. He received approval to subdivide the tract into two parcels and presented a subdivision plan for one tract. He requested a variance from the ordinance that all lots front on a public street or an improved private street. The zoning hearing board advised him that a variance was not needed and sent him to appellant Heidelberg Township Board of Supervisors for approval. Appellant denied the application for subdivision for failure to meet the dictates of Heidelberg Township Subdivision and Land Development Ordinance § 509(b). The trial court reversed the order holding that the application of the ordinance caused an unlawful deprivation of property without compensation and ordered appellant to approve the subdivision plan. On appeal the court reversed because it found that appellee was given adequate notice of the approval denial and that the refusal, although contrary to the zoning board's determination that a variance was not required, was not an abuse of discretion. The court found that the denial did not result in an unconstitutional deprivation of property without compensation when it did not make the property useless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and denied appellee individual's application for subdivision of lots because there was proper notice of the denial of approval of his subdivision plan, the denial was not an abuse of discretion, and the denial did not result in an unconstitutional deprivation of appellee's property without compensation when the property was not rendered useless by application of the ordinance.

 

721 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Taxpayers of Carbondale v. Carbondale


No. 2139 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


123 Pa. Commw. 20; 553 A.2d 119; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 29


September 12, 1988, Argued  
January 20, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County, in the case of Taxpayers of the City of Carbondale, et al. v. City of Carbondale, No. 87 Equity 1.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Decree Nisi reinstated. Care remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania), which vacated a decree nisi that enjoined appellee city from paying monies to the chief of police or the police pension fund on behalf of the chief of police.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers filed an equity action to enjoin appellee city from paying monies to the chief of police. The trial court vacated the chancellor's decree nisi. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order and reinstated the decree nisi. The court held that though appellants did not show that they had a direct, immediate, and substantial interest in their claim, they met the required special circumstances that gave them standing to challenge the constitutionality of the award of veteran's points under Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7103(b). The court found that redress through another channel was unavailable and that there were no other persons better situated to assert the claim. The court found that the veteran's points awarded to the chief of police under § 7103(b) were given before his examination was scored and that there were no established grounds for revoking such points. The court held that § 7103(b) granted a special privilege to the chief of police in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, § 7, which prohibited irrevocable grants of special privileges and immunities. The court remanded the case to the trial court for disposition of appellee's motion for post-trial relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order and reinstated the decree nisi that enjoined appellee city from paying any monies to the chief of police or the police pension fund on behalf of the chief of police. The court held that the proper special circumstances existed to give appellant taxpayers standing to challenge the statutory veteran-preference-points awarded to the chief of police for his civil service examination.

 

722 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania Builders Asso. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Revenue


No. 3551 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


122 Pa. Commw. 493; 552 A.2d 730; 1989 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 4


September 16, 1988, Argued  
January 6, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Jurisdiction in the case of Pennsylvania Builders Association; G. Keith Constructors, Inc.; David G. Heisey Development Company, Inc.; and David G. Heisey, Inc. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Revenue.



DISPOSITION: Petitioners' motion for summary judgment denied. Respondent's motion for summary judgment granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, builders and building association, and respondent Pennsylvania Department of Revenue filed cross-motions for summary judgment in petitioners' action seeking a declaration that a provision of the Realty Transfer Tax Article of the Tax Reform Code of 1971, 72 P.S. §§ 8101-C to 8112-C, which made some real estate improvement contracts taxable, was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner builders sold empty lots to buyers who entered into executory contracts with petitioners for the later construction of houses on those lots. Prior to the 1986 amendments to the Tax Reform Code, those buyers paid transfer tax only on the value of the lot while other buyers who purchased newly constructed homes, where the lot and the finished house were sold together, paid transfer tax on the value for both. The 1986 amendments to 72 P.S. §§ 8101-C to 8112-C imposed the transfer tax on petitioner builders' buyers for the value of the soon-to-be-built house as well as the lot. Petitioners claimed this method of determining value was invalid. The court decided the Department of Revenue's use of petitioners' executory contracts was a valid method of valuation for taxable transfers as defined in the transfer tax provisions. Petitioners' arrangement was a loophole properly closed by taxing all new home sales uniformly on the full monetary worth of the interest in real estate conveyed. The tax scheme met constitutional muster because there existed an adequate basis for classifying petitioners' construction contracts as part of the value of a bargained-for conveyance of land.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for respondent department of revenue was granted. Petitioner builders who sold lots and contracted for future building of houses did not invalidate the method of valuing real estate subject to transfer tax because the method required all home buyers to pay tax on the full consideration for both house and lot. Petitioners' contracts were not taxable, but they could properly be used to determine the value subject to tax.

Galena v. Commonwealth, Dep't of State, Bureau of Professional & Occupational Affairs


No. 501 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


122 Pa. Commw. 315; 551 A.2d 676; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 991


November 4, 1988, Argued  
December 23, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of State, Bureau of Professional and Occupational Affairs in the case of: In the Matter of the Automatic Suspension of the License to Practice Medicine and Surgery of Harold J. Galena, M.D., License No. MD-021398-E, No. 87-49-00599.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner doctor appealed an order from respondent State Board of Medicine, which mandated an automatic suspension of his license to practice medicine pursuant to the Medical Practice Act, 63 P.S. §§ 422.1-422.45 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner doctor held a license to practice medicine and surgery in the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. Petitioner was later found guilty of knowingly and intentionally distributing controlled substances outside the usual course of his professional practice. Respondent State Board of Medicine mandated an automatic suspension of petitioner's license to practice medicine pursuant to the Medical Practice Act (the Act), 63 P.S. §§ 422.1-422.45 (1985). Petitioner appealed respondent's order. The court affirmed respondent's order. The court found that respondent did not have discretion under the Act to suspend petitioner's license for any period of less than 10 years. The court found that the Act specifically provided for both the regulation of the medical profession and the penalties for failing to abide by those regulations. The court determined that under 63 P.S. § 422.22(b), the requirement of good moral character was a condition of licensure. The court concluded that 63 P.S. § 422.40(b) did not operate as an ex post facto law and that petitioner's constitutional rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order from respondent State Board of Medicine suspending petitioner doctor's medical license because respondent did not have discretion under the Medical Practice Act (the Act) to suspend petitioner's license for any period of less than 10 years. The court concluded that the automatic suspension provision of the Act did not operate as an ex post facto law and that petitioner's constitutional rights were not violated.

 

724 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Palyok v. West Mifflin


No. 1482 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


122 Pa. Commw. 25; 551 A.2d 622; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 946


May 27, 1988, Argued  
December 13, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Granted September 19, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, in the case of Michael Palyok v. Borough of West Mifflin and Jack Bergman, Theresa Corso, Joseph Mahoney and Irene Parkinson, members of West Mifflin Police Pension Fund, No. GD85-18231.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which granted summary judgment to appellee borough in appellant's action to require appellee to include appellant's overtime and extra work pay in its calculations for his retirement pension benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officer retired after contributing a portion of his salary, overtime, and extra work pay to a pension fund. Appellee borough refused to include the overtime and extra work pay in calculating his retirement benefits. Appellant filed a complaint in mandamus and both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted appellee's motion and denied appellant's motion. On review, the court affirmed. The court noted that appellant improperly filed the action in mandamus because appellee was performing its duty in paying appellant a pension. The court did not address appellant's extra work contributions because that pay was governed by a separate and distinct agreement. Appellant's overtime pay was properly left out of appellee's calculations because utilizing the uniform base salaries of eligible employees enabled municipalities, such as appellee, to predict with greater precision the amount of pension benefits, thus contributing to the maintenance of a stable fund. Appellant did not suffer an adverse unilateral modification in the retirement system because he had no right to an increased pension as a result of his contributions from his overtime pay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because appellee borough was not required to include appellant police officer's overtime pay in its calculations for his retirement pension because base rates were to be used to ensure uniformity and a stable pension system. Appellant's extra pay was not to be included either as that pay was governed by a separate agreement.

Pennsylvania Gamefowl Breeders Asso. v. Commonwealth


No. 917 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


122 Pa. Commw. 52; 551 A.2d 361; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 979


October 9, 1987, Argued  
December 8, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued September 16, 1988. Petition for Reargument Filed. Reconsideration Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original jurisdiction in the case of Pennsylvania Gamefowl Breeders Association, Bruce Kinsinger, President, and Jose Lopez, Jr. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, LeRoy Zimmerman, Attorney General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained and petition dismissed. Preliminary objections sustained. Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, gamefowl breeder association, filed a petition of review in the nature of a declaratory judgment in the court's original jurisdiction requesting that recent amendments to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511 be declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, gamefowl breeder association, filed a petition of review in the nature of a declaratory judgment in the court's original jurisdiction requesting that recent amendments to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511 be declared unconstitutional under the federal and state constitutions. The court dismissed the petition for review on the grounds that it did not present a controversy ripe for review and granted petitioner's request to amend the petition. Petitioner's amended petition for review in the nature of a declaratory judgment added additional respondents and alleged that petitioner's members were arrested and prosecuted for fighting waterfowl in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511. Stat. § 761 to consider the petition.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed with prejudice the amended petition filed by petitioners, gamefowl breeders association, because petitioners failed to allege a controversy with respondent, commonwealth parties, and dismissed the petition as against respondents, additional parties, for lack of original jurisdiction.

Nepa v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 2662 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


121 Pa. Commw. 532; 551 A.2d 354; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 926


October 6, 1988, Argued  
December 7, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Public Welfare, in the case of Appeal of: Nepa's Mountain View Manor, Docket No. 34-87-013.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner personal care home administrator, appealed an order of the Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania), which denied the appeal of his home care license revocation.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner personal care home administrator, challenged an order which denied the appeal of his home care license revocation. A hearing examiner specifically found incidents of abusive conduct against the residents of the home. The court affirmed and held that its scope of review was limited, and that findings of fact, and the credibility of witnesses, was for the Director of the Office of Hearings and Appeals. Further, 62 P.S. § 1026(b)(4), (5) provided sufficient notice that a license would be revoked upon a finding of gross incompetence, negligence or misconduct in having operated the facility, or for having mistreated or abused individuals cared for in the facility. Even one instance of abuse was sufficient to have the license revoked. Petitioner's statement that he did not have adequate training to deal with the patients he received who suffered from mental problems was absolutely no excuse for the reprehensible manner in which he treated various residents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied petitioner personal care home administrator's appeal of his home care license revocation. Even one isolated incident of physical abuse of a resident on the part of the individual in charge was cause for revoking a personal care home license. Petitioner's lack of training in this area was absolutely no excuse for the conduct.

Menosky v. Commonwealth


No. 24 T.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


121 Pa. Commw. 464; 550 A.2d 1372; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 919


September 14, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
December 5, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, in the case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Wallace D. Menosky, No. S.A. 1027 of 1986.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the decision of the department of transportation in suspending appellant's operating privileges for one year for refusal to submit to a breathalyzer test pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1547(b).


OVERVIEW: Appellant licensee's van was found at the scene of an accident. Officers discovered that appellant was the owner of the van and went to his home to question him. Once at his home, the officers arrested him for drunk driving and appellant refused to take a breathalyzer. The department of transportation suspended his license pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1547(b). The trial court upheld the department's action. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the facts and circumstances were such that a reasonable person was able to conclude that appellant was driving while intoxicated. There was testimony that only 15 minutes transpired from the time the police received the radio call advising them of the accident until they interviewed appellant at his home. The individual who telephoned the police to report the accident stated that the man involved in the accident appeared to be intoxicated. Appellee state properly offered the individual who reported the accident's out-of-court statement to explain why a police officer arrested appellant. The officer personally observed appellant's condition at his home and placed him under arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which upheld a decision of the department of transportation, which suspended appellant's driving privileges for one year because he refused to take a breathalyzer after he left the scene of an accident because the facts and circumstances were such that a reasonable person was able to conclude that appellant was driving while intoxicated.

Bartelme v. Commonwealth, DOT


No. 1132 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


128 Pa. Commw. 248; 563 A.2d 543; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1012


May 18, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
December 2, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Publication Ordered August 18, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Allegheny County Common Pleas Court, Honorable Robert A. Doyle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Having found no constitutional violation, we affirm the trial court's order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's driver's license suspension appeal, in favor of appellee state driver's licensing bureau.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped appellant driver while he was operating his car. The office noted appellant's slurred speech and a strong odor of alcohol on appellant's breath. After appellant was notified he was being placed under arrest, he was transported to a local hospital for a blood test to determine his blood alcoholic level. When appellant refused the test, he was advised that his refusal would result in a one year suspension of his driving privileges. The court affirmed the order of the lower court that dismissed a driver's license suspension appeal, in favor of appellee state driver's licensing bureau, because the only fact necessary to the administrative determination suspending driving privileges was appellant's refusal to comply with the blood test request after being taken into custody. Moreover, the police officer had a reasonable belief that appellant was driving while under the influence of alcohol. The court held that the township's policy of requiring a blood test among the three enumerated chemical tests under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1547 was not unconstitutional because § 1547 allowed, rather than required, the use of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that dismissed a driver's license suspension appeal, in favor of appellee state driver's licensing bureau, because a police officer had a reasonable belief that appellant driver was under the influence of alcohol. The court held that a township's policy of requiring a blood test was constitutional because the statute allowed, not required, the use of discretion.

Gondelman v. Commonwealth


No. 1420 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


120 Pa. Commw. 624; 550 A.2d 814; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 856; 48 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 420


October 5, 1988, Argued  
November 3, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Harold Gondelman, on his own behalf and on behalf of all others similarly situated v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Petitioners' Motion for Summary Relief denied. Respondent's Preliminary Objections overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a complaint for declaratory judgment, seeking to have Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b), which mandates retirement of all judges at age 70, declared unconstitutional, and both petitioner and intervenor judges filed a motion for summary relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed a declaratory action challenging the constitutionality of Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b), which mandated the retirement of all judges at age 70. Defendant commonwealth raised certain preliminary objections. Intervenor judges then appeared in the action with the parties' consent. Petitioner and intervenors filed a motion for summary relief. The court overruled defendant's objections, and denied the motion for summary relief. The court held that Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b), did not violate Pa. Const. art. I, § 1. The court held that Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b), did not discriminate against judges in the exercise of a civil right under Pa. Const. art. I, § 25. The court held that elected judges in Pennsylvania were excluded from the protection of the Age Discrimination in Employment Act. However, the court held that the petition did state a claim insofar as it alleged that Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b), violated the due process and equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and that issues of material fact existed as to that claim.


OUTCOME: The court overruled defendant Commonwealth's objections and denied petitioner's and intervenor judges' motion for summary relief, because petitioner and intervenors stated a claim upon which relief could be granted when they argued that the state constitutional provision mandating judges' retirement at age 70 violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment, but issues of material fact remained as to that claim.
