Slovak-American Citizens Club v. Commonwealth


No. 683 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


120 Pa. Commw. 528; 549 A.2d 251; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 833


April 22, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
October 20, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County in the case of Slovak-American Citizens Club of Oakview v. Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board, No. A-38, Pages 232-85.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant club challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the orders of appellee Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board. The first order suspended appellant's liquor license for improper record-keeping under 47 P.S. §4-493(12), and the second order revoked appellant's liquor license for sale of alcoholic beverages to a non-member in violation of 47 P.S. § 4-406(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant club was charged with failing to maintain records under 47 P.S. § 4-493(12) and with sale of alcohol to a non-member under 47 P.S. § 4-406(a). Appellant was issued a 30 day suspension for one violation and a revocation for the other violation. Appellant sought review and the trial court affirmed appellee Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board's decision. Appellant again sought review and contended that 47 P.S. 4-493(12) was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed and found that difficulty in ascertaining whether a violation falls under statutory language did not necessarily render the statute unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court found that the "catch-all" provision of § 4-493(12) afforded sufficient warning as the prohibited behavior. The court found that appellant was not subjected to double jeopardy because there was no criminal trial. The court found that 47 P.S. § 4-471 did not require that appellant receive actual notice of the alleged violations. Finally, the court found that there was substantial evidence to support the finding that appellant served liquor to a non-member.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which affirmed appellee Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board's decision to revoke appellant club's liquor license because the "catch-all" statute on violations was not unconstitutionally vague, and substantial evidence supported the finding that appellant served alcohol to a non-member.

 

731 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Ritter v. Commonwealth


No. 928 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


120 Pa. Commw. 374; 548 A.2d 1317; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 808


June 15, 1988, Argued  
October 13, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Karen A. Ritter, Babette Josephs and Andrew J. Carn, State Representatives v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and the Honorable Robert Casey, as Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Petitioners' motion for summary judgment denied; respondents' motions for summary judgment granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state representatives filed suit against respondent state and governor, arguing that passage of a bill relating to underage drinking, prisoner litigation, drug trafficking, littering, and abortion violated Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 1, 2, and 3 in that the bill's original purpose was altered, the amendments were not referred to committee, and the bill contained more than one subject. Both parties sought summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court granted respondent state and governor's motion for summary judgment in an action filed by petitioner state representatives, who argued that passage of a bill relating to underage drinking, prisoner litigation, drug trafficking, littering, and abortion violated Pa. Const. art. III. After finding that petitioners had standing to challenge the bill because they alleged that the procedures used to enact it interfered with their rights and duties as legislators, the court held that passage of the bill did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 1. It rejected petitioners' argument that the bill, which originally dealt with underage drinking, had been so altered as to change its original purpose, writing that the permissible scope of amendments to a bill was extremely broad and that the final form of the bill clearly stated its contents. It held that the bill did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, writing that it embraced a single subject, amendments to the penal code. It declined to review petitioners' argument that the bill violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 2 because the amendments were not referred to committee, writing that doing so would interfere in a legislative matter.


OUTCOME: Finding that passage of a bill dealing with underage drinking, prisoner litigation, drug trafficking, littering, and abortion did not violate the state constitution, the court granted summary judgment to respondent state and governor in an action filed by petitioner state representatives.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant billboard advertiser sought review of two orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania) that affirmed appellee zoning hearing board's decision to deny appellant variances to erect two outdoor billboards, arguing that it qualified for certain height and size variances under a municipal zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The trial court issued two orders that affirmed appellee zoning board's decision to deny appellant billboard advertiser variances to erect two outdoor billboards. Martin v. Haggerty


No. 325 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


120 Pa. Commw. 134; 548 A.2d 371; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 785


June 13, 1988, Argued  
September 29, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Thomas Martin and Edward Bernard Rosenfeld v. James J. Haggerty, Secretary of State of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; William P. Boehm, Commissioner of the Elections Bureau; David S. Owens, Jr., Corrections Commissioner; Glenn R. Jeffes, former Corrections Commissioner; and LeRoy S. Zimmerman, Attorney General.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates sought a declaratory judgment in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania, arguing that they had the right to register and vote because they were qualified electors pursuant to Pa. Const. art. VII, § 1, and 25 P.S. §§ 2602(w), 3146.1 (1988), and that exempting them from the definition of "qualified absentee elector" solely because they were prison inmates was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmates sought a declaratory judgment that they had the right to register and vote under the state constitution and requested injunctive relief which would have enabled them to do so. Petitioners contended that because they were qualified electors pursuant to Pa. Const. art. VII, § 1, the statutes exempting them from the definition of "qualified absentee elector," 25 P.S. §§ 2602(w), 3146.1 (1988), were unconstitutional. The court held that the provisions of the election code which prevented convicted felons from voting by absentee ballot did not violate the state constitution because the legislature had the power to except persons confined in a penal institution from the class of qualified electors. Additionally, prisoners who had been deprived of their liberty by society did not have a right to be transported to their regular polling places to register and to vote, nor did they have a right to compel the state to provide them with registration and polling places within the confines of their respective state correctional institutions. Finding that the petition for review failed to state a cause of action, the court dismissed the petition with prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition with prejudice because provisions of the election code excepting persons confined in a penal institution from the definition of "qualified absentee elector" did not violate the state constitution. Petitioner inmates did not have a right to be transported to their regular polling places, and petitioners did they have a right to registration and polling places inside correctional institutions.

 

734 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


McAdoo v. Lawn Specialties


No. 67 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


120 Pa. Commw. 120; 547 A.2d 1297; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 771


April 21, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
September 28, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County in the case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Lawn Specialties, No. 1584-1987.



DISPOSITION: Motion to quash denied. Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant borough sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County (Pennsylvania) that found appellant's ordinance was preempted by state law and found appellee lawn care service not guilty of violating the ordinance. Appellee filed a motion to quash the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant borough issued a fine against appellee lawn care service for failing to obtain a license from appellant before applying chemicals to lawns within appellant's boundaries. The lower court reversed the fine and found that the state had preempted the field of regulation. The court affirmed the decision that appellant's ordinance was preempted by state regulation based on 3 Pa. Stat. § 111.57(b) that specifically reserved the area for state regulation. The court denied appellee's motion to quash the appeal because appellant's ordinance did not have to be treated as a criminal matter for appeal purposes, because only a fine was possible, not incarceration.


OUTCOME: A lower court decision that found appellant borough's ordinance was preempted by state law and found appellee lawn care service not guilty of violating the ordinance was affirmed because the state statute clearly reserved the field for state control. The court denied appellee's motion to quash because the ordinance only provided for a fine, not incarceration, so the appeal did not have to be treated as a criminal appeal.

Roman Catholic Archdiocese v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania Human Relations Com.


No. 395 Miscellaneous Docket No. 4


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


119 Pa. Commw. 445; 548 A.2d 328; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 737


June 15, 1988, Argued  
September 15, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Denied December 14, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Orders of the Motions Commissioner of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, in the cases of Shirley Harris, on behalf of her minor daughter, Catrina Harris v. John W. Hallahan High School, Docket No. P-2175; Vernell L. Sebrell, on behalf of his minor son, Philip Sebrell v. St. Stephen's School, Docket No. P-2416; Jose Torres, on behalf of his minor son, Michael Torres v. Northeast Catholic High School for Boys, Docket No. P-2636, and Delores T. Martin, on behalf of her minor daughter, Tonya James and others similarly situated v. Lansdale Catholic High School, Docket No. P-2691, dated November 23, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Catholic schools sought review of orders from appellee Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, which denied appellants' motions to dismiss complaints filed by appellee parents alleging racial discrimination toward their children in violation of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 954.


OVERVIEW: Appellee parents filed complaints against appellant Catholic schools alleging racial and ethnic discrimination toward their children who were students at appellant schools. Appellee parents asserted violation of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act (the act), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 954. Appellee human relations commission denied appellants' motions to dismiss the complaints. Appellee commission concluded that appellants did not fit within the exclusion for "distinctly private" accommodations under § 954 because students who were not Catholic were admitted into appellants' schools. The court reversed the orders, holding that appellants were not "public accommodations" as defined in § 954(1) and, therefore, not subject to civil rights law scrutiny. The court concluded that the religious orientation of appellants made them "distinctly private." The court rejected appellees' argument that the act listed schools as within the purview of the public accommodation sections without limitation or qualification as to private or sectarian schools.


OUTCOME: The court reversed orders from appellee Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission which denied appellant Catholic schools' motions to dismiss complaints filed by appellee parents pursuant to the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act (the act). The court concluded that civil rights complaints by Catholic school students were not within the purview of the act because appellants were not "public accommodations" as defined in the act.

 

736 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Bradley v. Casey


No. 1573 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


119 Pa. Commw. 180; 547 A.2d 455; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 702


August 18, 1988, Heard  
August 26, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Amended September 19, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Jurisdiction in the case of Honorable Edward J. Bradley et al., and Honorable W. Wilson Goode et al. v. Honorable Robert P. Casey et al.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Action dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county judges and intervenor city officials brought a complaint in mandamus to compel defendant commonwealth officials to disburse funds necessary for the operation of the Philadelphia County Common Pleas Court system. Defendants filed preliminary objections to the suit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county judges, who were responsible for court system administration, filed an action in mandamus against defendant commonwealth officials. Plaintiffs sought relief in the nature of compliance by defendants with the commonwealth supreme court's decision that directed the general assembly to enact appropriate county court funding legislation. City officials intervened as party-plaintiffs. The court sustained defendants' preliminary objections and dismissed the action, finding that plaintiffs' complaint failed to meet the requirements for an action in mandamus and that plaintiffs lacked standing to bring the suit. The court determined that the supreme court's directive did not compel performance by the general assembly within a specified time and, thus, there was no present obligation to perform. Because the supreme court's order was entered only seven months prior to plaintiffs' suit, the court determined there was no unreasonable delay by defendants. The court also found that no present emergency for which defendants were responsible had arisen which jeopardized the efficient administration of justice and which necessitated plaintiffs' standing in the litigation.


OUTCOME: The court sustained defendant commonwealth officials' preliminary objections to a mandamus action filed by plaintiff county judges and intervenor city officials. The court dismissed the action because the complaint seeking county court funding failed to meet the requirements for an action in mandamus and because plaintiffs and intervenors lacked standing to bring the suit.

 

737 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Federation of State Cultural & Educational Professionals v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Education


No. 544 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


119 Pa. Commw. 63; 546 A.2d 147; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 693


June 15, 1988, Argued  
August 22, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Federation of State Cultural and Educational Professionals, Pennsylvania State Education Association, Ross Blust and Geoffrey S. Lucas v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Education and Office of General Counsel, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Declaratory judgment rendered in favor of petitioners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state employees filed a motion for summary judgment in petitioner's action against respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Education, in their action for a declaratory judgment that the State Adverse Interest Act, 71 P.S. §§ 776.1-776.8, did not bar petitioners from supplemental employment with entities with which respondent had contracts.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner state employees were educators who wanted to teach night courses at various universities. Respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Education, denied their applications for approval, because respondent had contracts with the universities, and § 5 of the State Adverse Interest Act (Act), 71 P.S. § 776.5, stated that no employee could have an adverse interest in any contract with the state agency by which he was employed. Despite the fact that §§ 2(4), 2(2), of the Act, 71 P.S. §§ 776.2(4), 776.2(2), defined "adverse interest" and "contract" so as to encompass the prospective employment, the court granted petitioners' motion. Finding that the prospective employment was in no way actually adverse to respondent, the court relied on §§ 1921, 1922 of the Statutory Construction Act of 1972, 1 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1921, 1922, to construe the Act in a manner that avoided what the court considered an absurd or unintended result, and held that where the only connection between an employee's state employment and the requested supplemental employment consisted of unrelated contracts between the state and the proposed supplemental employer, the Act did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner state employees' motion for summary judgment and declared that the provisions of the Adverse Interest Act were inapplicable to requests for supplemental employment in the absence of a determination that an actual adverse interest was present, and ordered respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Education, to grant petitioners' requests for supplemental employment.

 

738 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Kennedy v. Commonwealth


No. 581 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


119 Pa. Commw. 24; 546 A.2d 733; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 677


June 15, 1988, Argued  
August 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of John Kennedy, citizen, and Bertram W. Olley and Daniel L. Schubert v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania et al.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections in nature and its members. Preliminary objections in nature of demurrers sustained. Complaint dismissed with prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the commonwealth and its legislature, demurred to a complaint filed by petitioners, citizens and taxpayers of the commonwealth, alleging that pay raises and unvouchered expense allowances enacted by and paid to respondent legislature were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent legislature argued that a complaint filed by petitioners, citizens and taxpayers, challenging on constitutional grounds an act granting legislators pay raises and expense allowances was barred by the Speech or Debate Clause of Pa. Const. art. II, § 15. The court agreed, explaining that the immunity of legislators must be absolute as to actions taken in their legitimate legislative sphere, not only as to the results of litigation against them but also to relieve them of the necessity of defending themselves. Moreover, the court agreed with respondent commonwealth's assertion that the complaint failed to state a cause of action. The increase in the unvouchered expense account afforded to current legislators did not violate Pa. Const. art. II, § 8, as this provision only barred increases in "salary," and such increases did not constitute compensation for services rendered. And the constitutional prohibition against voting on bills in which legislators had an interest only applied to interests of which other members were unaware. Finally, petitioners' failure to demonstrate any constitutional violation precluded a challenge to the nonseverability provision of the act.


OUTCOME: Demurrers filed by respondents, the commonwealth and its legislature, sustained in complaint filed by petitioners taxpayers alleging that future pay raises and current unvouchered expense allowances enacted by and to be paid to respondent legislators were unconstitutional, as respondent legislators enjoyed absolute immunity as to actions taken in their legislative sphere, and as expense increases were not constitutionally proscribed "salary."

Brasco v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Bd. (Gee Bee Furniture)


No. 2455 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


118 Pa. Commw. 564; 546 A.2d 717; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 660


March 21, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
August 15, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board, in the case of James Brasco, Jr. v. Gee Bee Furniture, No. A-87522.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed from an order from respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania) affirming the dismissal of employer's petition to terminate petitioner's benefits and reversing the penalty imposed upon employer under § 435 of the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act, 77 P.S. § 991.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant sustained a back injury at work and received workmen's compensation of total disability benefits for which employer filed a petition for termination with an affidavit of recovery. The court vacated the order of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board that affirmed a referee's dismissal of employer's petition to terminate the benefits and that reversed the referee's penalty imposed upon employer pursuant to § 435 of the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act (Act), 77 P.S. § 991. The court remanded the matter because it held that employer was entitled to a hearing under § 413 of the Act, 77 P.S. § 772. The court disagreed with respondent that no evidence existed to prove that the employer violated the Act. Respondent correctly ruled that the referee could not assess a penalty without first conducting a hearing. The court ruled that constitutional due process required both notice and a hearing before any penalty could be imposed. The court concluded that the record contained substantial evidence to support the referee's finding that the employer unlawfully obtained an automatic supersedeas with an improperly notarized affidavit.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board that affirmed the dismissal of employer's petition to terminate the benefits of petitioner claimant and that reversed the penalty imposed upon employer by law. The court remanded the matter because employer was entitled to notice and a hearing under the statute to determine if the employer violated the law, and if so, whether then to impose a penalty.

George Washington Motor Lodge Co. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Transp.

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


118 Pa. Commw. 552; 545 A.2d 493; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 658


June 14, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
August 12, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Transportation, in the case of In Re: George Washington Motor Lodge Company, Advertising Device Permit, T.R. 22, Whitehall Township, Lehigh County, No. 011 A.D. 1985, dated December 3, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner company appealed from an order of respondent Pennsylvania Department of Transportation denying petitioner's request for an advertising device permit pursuant to the Outdoor Advertising Control Act of 1971, 36 P.S. § 2718.106.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner company applied for an advertising device permit from respondent Pennsylvania Department of Transportation under the Outdoor Advertising Control Act of 1971 (Act), 36 P.S. § 2718.106. The court affirmed respondent's denial of petitioner's application under 67 Pa. Code § 445.4(b)(2)(i). The court held that nothing in the language of or about respondent's interpretation of § 445.4(b)(2)(i) was plainly erroneous and therefore respondent properly refused to issue a permit. The court rejected petitioner's interpretation of § 445.4(b)(2)(i) pursuant to the Act, 36 P.S. § 2718.105(c)(2)(v), because the legislature did not, and the court could not, insert the regulation into the Act. The court found no inconsistency in the prescribed manner of measuring the distance between signs. The court decided that petitioner's safety argument misinterpreted the Act's purpose and that petitioner failed to meet its heavy burden of proof to challenge respondent's exercise of its regulatory police power. Petitioner failed to prove that respondent's interpretation of 67 Pa. Code § 445.4(b)(2)(iii) was incorrect and that petitioner only suggested another possible construction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent Pennsylvania Department of Transportation that denied the request of petitioner company for an advertising device permit under the statute. The court held that neither the language of respondent's regulations nor its interpretations thereof were erroneous and hence respondent's refusal to issue a permit was proper. The court found that petitioner failed to carry its burdens of proof on its contentions.

Hill, as parent and natural guardian of Joanne L. Hill and Lucille A. Hill, minors v. Mark W. Kamppi, Avonia Farms, Inc., Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation and Winters & Flemming, Inc. v. Koch Asphalt Company, a division of Koch's Fuels, Inc., Koch's Fuels, Inc., a Delaware Corporation, Koch Industries, Inc., a Kansas Corporation, and Koch Materials Company, No. 4567-A-1986, and in the case of Merle Walters and Patricia Walters, his wife v. Mark W. Kamppi, Avonia Farms, Inc., Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, and Winters & Flemming, Inc. v. Koch Asphalt Company, a division of Koch's Fuels, Inc., Koch Fuels, Inc., a Delaware Corporation, Koch Industries, Inc., a Kansas Corporation, and Koch Materials Company, No. 123-A-1987.
Hill v. Kamppi, 1 Pa. D. & C.4th 142, 1987 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 7 (1987)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought consolidated review of orders of the Erie County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) which denied appellant's petition to intervene in actions which were filed by appellees, former employees and their families, in that court. The actions below arose out of a motor vehicle accident which occurred while appellee former employees were within the scope of their employment for appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employer filed petitions to intervene in tort actions filed by appellees, former employees and their families, seeking to establish a right of subrogation, reimbursement or set-off by reason of the workmen's compensation benefits paid to appellees against any sums payable as a result of the suit. The petitions were denied and appellant sought review of the trial court's decision. The court ruled that the Pennsylvania Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1701-1798, plainly prohibited subrogation or reimbursement from a claimant's tort recovery with respect to workers' compensation benefits. Appellant's challenge to the constitutionality of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1720 was also unsuccessful. The court ruled that the statute, which barred subrogation, was reasonable and bore a real and substantial relation to the object of the legislation. The court held that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1720 barred subrogation in the appellees' actions because the underlying actions clearly arose from the use of a motor vehicle and the theory of liability asserted against each defendant did not affect the nature of the action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order forbidding appellant employer to intervene and held that Pennsylvania's Financial Responsibility Law barred appellant's right to subrogation for workmen's compensation benefits paid to appellee former employees and their families.

American Federation of State, etc., Dist. Council 33, Local 159 v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania Labor Relations Bd.


Nos. 1401 C.D. 1986, 1675 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania

December 15, 1987, Argued  
August 1, 1988, Decided

Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board, Nos. 1842 May Term, 1985 and 4461 August Term, 1985, dated March 31, 1986.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant union challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the orders of appellee Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board dismissing charges of unfair labor practices filed by appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant union filed charges of unfair labor practices with appellee Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board related to representation of deputy sheriffs in the Philadelphia County Sheriff's office. Appellee dismissed the charges and appellant sought review. The trial court affirmed and appellant sought further review. The court first determined that there was substantial evidence in support of the findings by appellee and the trial court that the sheriff did not improperly influence the representation election. Instead, the only proscription was that the sheriff could not participate in the bargaining process. The decision of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision upholding the dismissal of appellant union's unfair labor practice charges was affirmed, as substantial evidence existed to support the findings of appellee Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board, and its decisions regarding a sheriff's role in appellant's representation election were reasonable and not capricious, arbitrary, or illegal.

Beers v. Commonwealth


Nos. 367 C.D. 1987, 404 C.D. 1987, 1754 C.D. 1987, 1764 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


118 Pa. Commw. 248; 546 A.2d 1260; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 611


December 14, 1987, Argued  
July 29, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted March 30, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review in the cases of Bonnie Beers (Token Claimant), No. B-255478; Pearlie M. Parker, No. B-255479; United Food and Commercial Workers Union, Local 1357 and Delores A. Wetzel, No. B-259400.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, petitioners, seasonal workers and union, appealed from the orders of respondent, Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, granting seasonal status to fruit or vegetable processing operations of employers pursuant to the Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 802.5. Petitioners alleged that the board erred in finding that 43 P.S. § 802.5 authorization and determination procedures were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Four employers were granted seasonal status under 43 P.S. § 802.5 for a processing operation of perishable fruits or vegetables in a fresh state. Judicially noting that perishable fruits or vegetables must be processed promptly and that the statute comports with common knowledge that weather conditions affect harvesting, the court concluded that "climatic conditions" made it impossible or impractical for the employers to carry on operations for more than 180 days. Portions of the employers' seasonal business were "functionally distinct" operations as certain equipment was used and operated by seasonal employees only when the seasonal operation was carried on. The statute did not violate the guarantees under Pa. Const. art. III, § 32, and the legislation was not enacted in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 1-4. The procedures set forth in 43 P.S. § 802.5 for seasonal determinations did not violate petitioners' constitutional right to procedural due process as such determination did not adjudicate petitioners' rights to collect benefits. Failure to post an application did not preclude a grant of seasonal status.


OUTCOME: The orders of respondent, Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Board, granting seasonal status to employers' fruit and vegetable procession operations were affirmed, because respondent properly found that climatic conditions made it impossible to carry on functionally distinct operations more than 180 days a year, and the governing statute and procedures complied with the mandates of state and federal constitutions.

Rhodes v. Laurel Highlands School Dist.


No. 1041 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


118 Pa. Commw. 119; 544 A.2d 562; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 583


March 24, 1988, Argued  
July 22, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Education in the case of George Rhodes, Jr. v. Laurel Highlands School District, Teacher Tenure Appeal, No. 10-86.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, tenured school teacher, sought review of an order of the Department of Education (Pennsylvania), which affirmed his dismissal by respondent, school district, for persistently and willfully violating the school laws and policies. Petitioner alleged that he did not have a fair hearing because he was denied procedural and substantive due process, and because the evidence was insufficient for dismissal.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, tenured school teacher, sought review of an order affirming his dismissal by respondent, school district, for violations of school laws and policies. Petitioner was dismissed for promoting his personal religious views in the classroom. Petitioner claimed respondent's refusal to answer interrogatories denied him procedural due process, and that because he had no idea what was prohibited with respect to teaching religion, because respondent failed to set forth a standard which was precise, his substantive due process rights were violated. The court held that there was no provision for discovery proceedings before a school board, and that because there had been conferences and correspondence regarding specific objections to petitioner's teaching of religion, he could not now say he did not understand what was prohibited. The court held that petitioner's repeated references in the classroom to Christianity, God, the devil and demons, exceeded the constitutional boundaries within which discourse about religion was permissible. Because there was substantial evidence to support the findings of fact by respondent, the order upholding the dismissal was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of petitioner, a tenured school teacher, by respondent school district was affirmed, because petitioners' repeated references in the classroom to Christianity, God, the devil, and demons, exceeded the constitutional boundaries within which discourse about religion was permissible. The court held there was sufficient evidence to support the findings of fact.

Chambers Dev. Co. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


No. 392 Miscellaneous Docket No. 4


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


118 Pa. Commw. 97; 545 A.2d 404; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 576


April 21, 1988, Argued  
July 21, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Environmental Resources, in the cases of William H. Martin, Inc. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources, EHB Docket No. 87-465-W, and Southern Alleghenies Disposal Service, Inc. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources, EHB Docket No. 87-466-W, dated December 11, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Board order affirmed. Injunction dissolved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner development company sought review of a decision of the Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), which denied petitioner's request for supersedeas and stay of an order from respondent Department of Environmental Resources placing limits on the daily volume of waste petitioner could process.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner development company appealed the decision of the Environmental Hearing Board, which denied its request for supersedeas and stay of a regulation from respondent Department of Environmental Resources limiting the amount of waste product it could process. On appeal, the court affirmed the order, holding that 25 Pa. Code § 21.78 was not invalid. The regulation was promulgated by an express grant of authority. The regulation was issued pursuant to proper procedure, and it was reasonable. The procedural promulgation of the regulation was not challenged, and the court held and presumed respondent acted properly in implementing the regulation. The court concluded that it was reasonable when viewed in light of the declaration of public policy set forth in 35 P.S. § 6018.102, to protect the public health, safety, and welfare, as the regulation intended to do just that. Petitioner negotiated the contracts with full knowledge of the interpretation of the daily volume limits in solid waste permits, and even negotiated clauses in the contracts to protect itself in the event action was taken to enforce the permit conditions.


OUTCOME: The order of the Environmental Hearing Board denying petitioner development company's supersedeas petition was affirmed, and the injunction pending appeal previously entered by the court and continued in effect was dissolved. The regulation of respondent Department of Environmental Regulation was found to be properly promulgated and applied to petitioner.

 

746 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


New Castle v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Bd. (Sallie)


No. 1335 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


118 Pa. Commw. 51; 546 A.2d 132; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 567


March 22, 1988, Argued  
July 20, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 12, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board in the case of Earl A. Sallie, Deceased, Nora Lee Sallie, Widow v. City of New Castle, No. A-91682.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer appealed from an order of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the award of fatal claim benefits rendered by its referee to respondent claimant, on the ground that respondent claimant's husband died as a result of a fatal disease he contracted from a co-worker while he was within the course of his employment, as set forth in 77 P.S. § 411(1).


OVERVIEW: Decedent husband died of complications from meningococcal septicemia. When decedent's co-workers were tested, one employee whom he had kissed on the cheek days before his death was found to be a carrier of the disease. On appeal from an award of fatal benefits to respondent claimant, the court held that decedent's act of goodwill toward his co-worker was neither foreign to his employment, nor did it constitute an abandonment thereof. The court thus found that decedent was within the course of employment when the event occurred which activated his injury and death as understood under 77 P.S. § 411(1). The court affirmed, holding that a disease contracted solely because a co-worker had communicated that disease was a compensable injury under the Act because the Act did not require added or peculiar risks, but simply compensated for injuries arising within the course of employment. Petitioner employer waived its claim of unconstitutionality by failing to raise the issue in its appeal to respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board. There was sufficient unequivocal medical testimony to show that decedent's fatal disease was contracted at work from a co-worker.


OUTCOME: The order of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board awarding fatal claim benefits to respondent claimant was affirmed on the ground that the fatal contagious disease contracted by decedent husband from a co-worker was an injury arising in the course of employment, and was therefore compensable. The referee's findings in this regard were supported by substantial evidence.

Tracey Mining Co. v. Commonwealth


No. 2283 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


117 Pa. Commw. 628; 544 A.2d 1075; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 554


February 23, 1988, Argued  
July 15, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction Appeal in the case of Tracey Mining Company, Twelve Vein Coal Company, G. B. Mining Coal Company, T.A.G. Coal Company, M & R Coal Company, Burnside Mining Company, Greenwood Mining, F & S Coal Company, Rothermel Coal Company, Burnrite Coal Company and Post Coal Company No. 2 v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources and Roger Hornberger, Acting Mine Manager, Bureau of Mining and Reclamation, and the Pennsylvania Environmental Hearing Board.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Case transferred to the Environmental Hearing Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent department filed preliminary objections to petitioner miners' action for injunctive relief, which sought to enjoin respondent from enforcing certain regulations promulgated pursuant to the Surface Mining Conservation and Reclamation Act, 52 P.S. § 1396.1 et seq., and the Clean Streams Law, 35 P.S. § 691.1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Respondent department created certain regulations to enforce the Surface Mining Conservation and Reclamation Act, 52 P.S. § 1396.1 et seq., and the Clean Streams Law, 35 P.S. § 691.1 et seq. Petitioner miners filed an action for injunctive relief that sought to enjoin respondent from enforcing such regulations and penalties. Petitioners contended that the regulations violated the statutes and failed to differentiate between bituminous and anthracite mining. Respondent filed objections alleging that the court did not have jurisdiction because petitioners did not challenge the regulations before the Environmental Hearing Board. The court sustained respondent's objections and transferred the action to the Board because petitioners failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. In addition, the issues involved were highly technical and factually complex so that the Board was better prepared to address such issues. The Board had superior expertise in the field. The court held that the right to a jury trial did not apply to administrative proceedings involving the environmental statutes in question.


OUTCOME: The court sustained respondent department's objections and transferred petitioner miners' action to the Environmental Hearing Board. Petitioners failed to exhaust their administrative remedies and should have first brought their action before the Board. The Board was better qualified to handle the technical environmental issues.

 

748 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Condemnation by Urban Redevelopment Auth.


No. 821 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


117 Pa. Commw. 475; 544 A.2d 87; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 530


March 23, 1988, Argued  
July 8, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, in the case of In the Matter of: Condemnation by Urban Redevelopment Authority of Pittsburgh of certain land in the twenty-second and twenty-third wards of the City of Pittsburgh, Allegheny County, Pennsylvania, redevelopment area No. 39 (North Shore) being property of: E-V Company, a partnership composed of Emil F. Kehr and Vincent E. Malone, or any other persons found to have an interest in the property, Keller Office Equipment Company, Pittsburgh Harley Davidson, Inc., formerly Allegheny County Distributors, Inc., a Pennsylvania Corporation, or any other person found to have an interest in the property, No. G.D. 81-27642.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condemnees sought review from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which overruled their preliminary objections to the declaration of taking filed by the Urban Redevelopment Authority of Pittsburgh.


OVERVIEW: Appellant condemnees purchased the subject property without notice that a certificate of blight had been issued in 1964. The Urban Redevelopment Authority of Pittsburgh (Authority) was authorized to take the property in 1972 and began taking proceedings in 1981. The court affirmed the decision to overrule appellants' objection to the Authority's taking of their property. Appellants' contention that the hearing provided after the declaration of taking did not satisfy due process was without merit. Appellants were given the opportunity to meet their burden of proving that the blight certification was arbitrary, but failed to do so. The lapse of time between taking and blight certification did not so disable appellants from proving their allegations as to rise to the level of a constitutional violation. The Authority could not be held to have abandoned the redevelopment project because renewal was a slow process. The Authority presented uncontradicted evidence of blight and it could not be said that the determination went stale. Certification of blight was not subject to the Local Agency Law, 2 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 105, 551-555, 751-754.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision to overrule appellant condemnees' preliminary objections to the declaration of taking filed by the Urban Redevelopment Authority of Pittsburgh. Appellants were not denied due process because they were given ample opportunity to contest the certification of blight, but did not do so. The Authority did not abandon the redevelopment project, and the blight certification did not go stale.

Kallmann v. Carlisle Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 1499 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


117 Pa. Commw. 499; 543 A.2d 1273; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 533


April 19, 1988, Argued  
July 8, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for reargument filed and denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, in the case of Diane U. Kallmann and M. Letitia Harris v. Carlisle Zoning Hearing Board, Arkansas Best Freight Systems, Inc., and Farmers Trust Company, No. 945 Civil 1987.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant objectors challenged a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania) that dismissed their declaratory judgment action, which challenged appellee board's decision to grant appellee company a variance, for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellee company wanted to pave over certain land. A zoning ordinance regulated the percentage of land that could be paved. Appellee company filed a variance application with appellee board to increase the percentage. A hearing was held on such issue, and appellee board granted the application. Appellant objectors initiated a declaratory judgment action alleging that appellee board gave insufficient hearing notice. The trial court dismissed appellant's complaint for lack of jurisdiction because appellant's action was untimely filed under 53 P.S. § 10915. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. The court held that appellants' declaratory judgment action was a disguised appeal. Appellants' action did not present the complexity of issues that made declaratory judgment appropriate. Appellants made no claim regarding the constitutionality of appellee board's notice procedure, nor did they challenge the constitutionality of appellee board's enabling legislation. Appellants' action was merely an appeal of appellee board's decision and was not filed within 30 days of such decision as required by § 10915.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision dismissing appellant objectors' declaratory judgment action for lack of jurisdiction because the action was untimely filed. The action was a disguised appeal from appellee board's decision granting appellee company a variance and should have been filed within 30 days of such decision.

BethEnergy Mines, Inc. v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Bd. (Sadvary)


No. 1826 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


117 Pa. Commw. 465; 543 A.2d 1268; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 543


April 5, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
July 6, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board in the case of Steve Sadvary, Deceased, Alice Sadvary, Widow v. BethEnergy Mines, Inc., No. Misc. 4365.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer challenged the decision of the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board which dismissed its petition alleging that respondent widow had entered into a meretricious relationship and should therefore have her widow's benefits terminated under § 307(7) of the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act, 77 P. S. § 562.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employer sought review of respondent Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board's order which dismissed its petition alleging that respondent widow had entered into a meretricious relationship and should therefore have her widow's benefits terminated under § 307(7) of the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act, 77 P. S. § 562. Respondent board found that although respondent widow had entered into such a relationship, her age, lack of work experience and residence in an economically depressed area rendered her dependent upon the benefits and refused to terminate her benefits. On appeal, petitioner claimed that respondent board lacked discretionary authority under § 307(7) to deny a petition where petitioner proved its case. The court agreed and reversed respondent board's order. Respondent lacked authority to order a mere suspension instead of a termination and also lacked the authority to choose not to impose termination because the legislature chose to make as a requirement of continued benefits that a widow forgo a meretricious relationship.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of respondent Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board, which dismissed petitioner employer's complaint alleging that respondent widow had entered into a meretricious relationship and should therefore have her widow's benefits terminated. Under the statute respondent board lacked the discretionary authority to refuse to terminate a widow's benefits when she had engaged in a meretricious relationship.

Gatti v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 2214 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


117 Pa. Commw. 399; 543 A.2d 622; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 520


April 18, 1988, Argued  
June 29, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lehigh County, in the case of Robert J. Gatti and Mann Homes, Inc. v. Zoning Hearing Board of Salisbury Township, No. 86-C-1882.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the order from the Court of Common Pleas, Lehigh County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order granting a variance request and giving appellee radio station permission to expand the building, and which remanded with respect to a new broadcasting tower.


OVERVIEW: Appellee radio station requested a variance in order to expand its building a build a broadcasting tower, and appellant property owner objected to appellee's plans. The Zoning Hearing Board of Salisbury Township (Board) gave appellee permission to expand the building and construct a tower, and the trial court affirmed the variance for the expansion of the building, but remanded on the issue of the broadcasting tower. On appeal, the court held that appellee's expansion would not extend the nonconforming use into any new area, but into an area already devoted to the use. The court held that where a variance was minor it might be granted even if the traditional grounds for a variance had not been met, and that the Board had substantial evidence to support its decision and committed no abuse of discretion or error of law. The court affirmed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court that affirmed an order granting a variance request giving appellee radio station permission to expand the building and remanded with respect to a new broadcasting tower. The court held that the expansion would not have extended the nonconforming use into any new area, the variance granted was minor, and there was substantial evidence supporting the issuance of the variance.

LCN Real Estate, Inc. v. Wyoming


No. 1903 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


117 Pa. Commw. 260; 544 A.2d 1053; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 492


April 18, 1988, Argued  
June 23, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, in the case of LCN Real Estate, Inc., Wyoming Historical and Geological Society, Wyoming Plaza Realty Company, Midway Associates, Dr. Joseph Lapatofsky, John Schifano, Joan Mesaros, James Pizano, Marvell Kitchens, Inc., Francis Capitano, Christy Morris, Baltimore Life Insurance Co. v. Borough of Wyoming, No. 129-E of 1986.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the orders from the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the preliminary objections of appellee borough and dismissed its complaint in equity seeking to enjoin appellee from enforcing an ordinance providing for the assessment of certain amounts against its property for the cost of sewer construction and to prevent appellee from filing liens based on those assessments.


OVERVIEW: The department of environmental resources directed appellee borough to build or expand a public sewer system. Appellants' properties were located in that area. Appellee built the system. Appellee adopted an ordinance that adopted tappage fees and front foot assessment costs. Appellee assessed appellants for those costs. Appellants alleged that appellee did not take steps to reduce the cost of the project and that they were unfairly assessed. The lower court issued an order dismissing appellants' complaint in equity which sought to enjoin appellee from enforcing an ordinance providing for the assessment of certain amounts against its property for the cost of sewer construction and to prevent appellee from filing liens based on those assessments. The court affirmed the lower court's decision because appellants failed to make a showing of any irreparable harm that would have befallen them by virtue of the existence of the liens while their challenges to the ordinance were adjudicated in the scire facias proceedings or by virtue of their pursuing the available statutory means for removing the liens; thus, the statutory remedies were not inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's rejection of the equity proceeding which sought to enjoin appellee borough from enforcing an ordinance for the assessment of certain amounts against its property for the cost of sewer construction and to prevent appellee from filing liens based on those assessments because appellants failed to show that they would have suffered irreparable harm. Thus, the lower court correctly declined to proceed in equity.

In re 1983 Audit Report of Beharry


Nos. 2780 C.D. 1986, 2880 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


116 Pa. Commw. 613; 544 A.2d 514; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 465


December 16, 1987, Argued  
June 8, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County, in the cases of In Re: 1983 Audit Report of Patricia A. Beharry, Controller, No. 19 April 1984; In Re: 1984 Audit Report of Patricia A. Beharry, Controller, No. 19 April 1985, and In Re: 1985 Washington County Annual Financial Report Surcharge, No. 1676 of 1986.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross-appellant county commissioners challenged the constitutionality of 16 P.S. §§ 1730 and 1731, and appellant controller and cross-appellants challenged the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County (Pennsylvania), that found 16 P.S. § 1752 was a prerequisite for appellant's imposition of a surcharge, and sustained a surcharge for a purchase by cross-appellants that was not within the exception of 16 P.S. § 1802(h)(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant controller assessed surcharges against cross-appellant county commissioners pursuant to 16 P.S. § 1730. Cross-appellant challenged the propriety of the surcharges pursuant to 16 P.S. § 1731. The trial court dismissed the surcharges because appellant failed to issue a refusal to pay in accordance with 16 P.S. § 1752 but sustained the surcharge for cross-appellants' purchase of a phone system without public bidding because it was not within the exception of 16 P.S. § 1802(h)(3). Appellant and cross-appellants sought review. Cross-appellants challenged the constitutionality of §§ 1730 and 1731. The court found that the public bidding exception in § 1802(h)(3) was inapplicable to cross-appellant's purchase. The appellate court found that § 1730 survived a due process challenge but § 1731 violated equal protection because it did not limit cross-appellants' liability to the actual loss incurred. The court vacated that portion of the trial court's order that sustained the surcharge on the phone system and remanded the case. Even though imposition of the surcharge was constitutionally permissible, the amount of the surcharge imposed violated equal protection.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated and remanded that portion of the trial court's order that sustained the surcharge imposed on cross-appellant county commissioners for the purchase of a phone system. Even though imposition of the surcharge by appellant controller was constitutionally permissible, the amount of the surcharge imposed violated equal protection because it did not limit cross-appellants' liability to the actual loss incurred.

Rosler v. Commonwealth, Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


No. 551 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


116 Pa. Commw. 604; 542 A.2d 624; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 461


January 6, 1988, Submitted on Briefs  
June 7, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, in the case of In Re: Claim of Daniel T. Rosler, No. B-255901.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of the decision of respondent, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the referee's determination that petitioner was ineligible for benefits for failure to meet the financial eligibility requirements of 43 P.S. § 804.


OVERVIEW: The Office of Employment Security denied petitioner claimant's application for unemployment compensation benefits and petitioner appealed. At a hearing before a referee, a military document evidencing petitioner's discharge from the U.S. Navy for other than honorable conditions was introduced. The referee affirmed, concluding that under 5 U.S.C.S. § 8521, petitioner's wages could not have been considered for unemployment compensation purposes due to his discharge for other than honorable conditions, and, as a result, petitioner was financially ineligible for benefits under 43 P.S. § 804. On appeal, respondent, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, affirmed. Petitioner sought review and the court affirmed, holding that respondent's denial of benefits did not violate petitioner's constitutional rights to equal protection or substantive due process. The denial of benefits to persons discharged for other than honorable conditions was rationally based on the state's legitimate interest in providing benefits to citizens who became unemployed through no fault of their own.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, denying benefits to petitioner claimant. Petitioner was financially ineligible to receive unemployment compensation benefits because of his discharge from the U.S. Navy under other than honorable conditions. Also, the application of unemployment compensation statutes did not violate the due process or equal protection clauses of the U.S. Constitution.

Fischer v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 896 C.D. 1988


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


116 Pa. Commw. 437; 543 A.2d 177; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 445


May 5, 1988, Heard  
May 31, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of JoAnne Fischer, Susan Roe, suing on behalf of themselves and all others similarly situated, Women Organized Against Rape, Concern for Health Options, Information, Care and Education, suing on behalf of themselves and all others similarly situated, Dr. Kaighn Smith and Elizabeth Blackwell Health Center for Women v. Department of Public Welfare, John White, Eileen M. Schoen and Robert Casey.



DISPOSITION: Motion for preliminary injunction denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, individuals and organizations representing rape victims' interests, filed a motion for preliminary injunction against the commonwealth in a trial court (Pennsylvania) to enjoin enforcement of the provisions of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3202(c) that amended the Abortion Control Act, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3201-3220.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, individuals and organizations representing rape victims' interests, sought to enjoin enforcement of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3215(c)(2), (3) and 3215(j)(1)-(3) (Act 31). The act prohibited government subsidization of abortions except where pregnancy was caused by rape or incest and the victim personally reported the incident to a law enforcement or child protective agency prior to the medical procedure. Petitioners argued that Act 31 was unconstitutional because it required disclosure of personal matters protected by the constitutional right to privacy. Pa. Const. art. I, § 1. The commonwealth asserted that the purpose of the act was to promote the commonwealth's interests in prosecuting perpetrators of crime and in deterring future crime and to enable it to determine whether public funds were being expended in an appropriate and lawful manner. In denying the petition for relief, the court found that although the individual right was important and valid, the government right was superior.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for a preliminary injunction filed by petitioners, individuals and organizations representing rape victims' interests, which asked the court to enjoin the commonwealth from enforcing Act 31. The court found that if an injunction were issued, the harm would be greater to the general public than to petitioners.

In re Appeal from Annual Audit & Fin. Report


Nos. 2387 C.D. 1986, 2021 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


116 Pa. Commw. 381; 543 A.2d 171; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 415


March 21, 1988, Argued  
May 26, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, in the case of In Re: An Appeal from the Annual Audit and Financial Report of the Township of Penn, Westmoreland County, Pennsylvania, for the year 1984, No. 13 Civil 1985.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township treasurer sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment against appellant in a township's appeal to its annual audit and financial report.


OVERVIEW: In an appeal to its annual audit and financial report, a township raised the issue that appellant township treasurer received for his services as treasurer and tax collector compensation exceeding $ 10,000, contrary to the Local Tax Collection Law (law) § 34, 72 P.S. § 5511.34. The trial court entered judgment against appellant in the amount of approximately $ 9,600. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court rejected appellant's argument that § 34 was a local or special law regulating the affairs of townships and thus a violation of Pa. Const. art. III, § 32. Section 34 had statewide application in that it applied to townships of the first class throughout the commonwealth. The court also held that § 34 did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 3. The title of the law clearly alerted a reasonable person that the law related to collection of taxes and was conferring powers on tax collectors. Implicit in the title was the power of a tax collector to receive compensation. The court held that the $ 10,000 limitation of § 34 would apply to moneys received by appellant but assessed and collected by others pursuant to the Local Tax Enabling Act, 53 P.S. §§ 6901-6924.


OUTCOME: The judgment against appellant township-treasurer in a township's appeal to its annual audit and financial report was affirmed. The section of the Local Tax Collection Law that imposed a $ 10,000 limitation on appellant's compensation did not violate the Pennsylvania Constitution, and the limitation would apply to moneys received by appellant but assessed and collected by others pursuant to the Local Tax Enabling Act.

Blosenski Disposal Service v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


No. 832 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


116 Pa. Commw. 315; 543 A.2d 159; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 423; 19 ELR 21324


February 22, 1988, Argued  
May 24, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for reargument filed and denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, in the case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources v. Blosenski Disposal Service, Nos. 183-82, 184-82.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant disposal service sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania). The order denied appellant's post-trial motions for arrest of judgment and for a new trial after appellant was found guilty of violations pertaining to unlawful conduct under 35 P.S. §§ 6018.610(2), 6018.610(4), of the Solid Waste Management Act.


OVERVIEW: An agent of appellee Department of Environmental Resources issued citations to appellant disposal service for violations of 25 Pa. Code § 75.21(a), which pertained to unlawful conduct under sections of the Solid Waste Management Act (Act). The sections were 35 P.S. § 6018.610(2), which prohibited operating or utilizing a solid waste processing facility without a permit, and 35 P.S. § 6018.610(4), which prohibited the use of land as a municipal solid waste processing area without a permit. Appellant was found guilty of the violations, and appellant's post-trial motions for arrest of judgment and for a new trial were denied. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court found the evidence sufficient. The agent's eyewitness testimony was not so weak and inconclusive as to warrant an arrest of judgment. The court held that §§ 6018.610(2), 6018.610(4) encompassed the act of "depositing" solid waste if it is in violation of the regulations of appellee. The agent's warrantless entry onto appellant's property did not violate U.S. Const. amend. IV. The entry was made in reliance on a section of the Act that, at the time of the entry, was presumed to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant disposal service's motion for arrest of judgment and for a new trial was affirmed because the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding of guilt, sections of the Solid Waste Management Act prohibited the depositing of solid waste in violation of appellee Department of Environmental Resources regulations, and an agent of appellee's warrantless entry onto appellant's property was not unconstitutional.

Gardner v. Jenkins


No. 903 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


116 Pa. Commw. 107; 541 A.2d 406; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 350


June 10, 1987, Submitted on Briefs  
May 11, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for reargument filed and denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, in the case of Irving Gardner v. Frank Jenkins, Sheriff of Montgomery County, No. 84-12443.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania) which dismissed his complaint in mandamus against appellee sheriff of Montgomery County who refused to issue appellant a license to carry a concealed weapon pursuant to the Pennsylvania Uniform Firearms Act, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6109 on the ground that appellant was not a "suitable person."


OVERVIEW: Appellee sheriff denied appellant's application for a license to carry a concealed weapon. The trial court found appellant pulled a gun from his holster, waved it about, and said that this is how he gets his work done. Appellant challenged the trial court's dismissal of his mandamus action in which he sought to compel appellee to issue a license. On appeal, the court found the legislature's intent in the Pennsylvania Uniform Firearms Act, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6109 was to make the issuance of a firearms license not mandatory, but discretionary. Appellee was empowered to exercise judgment in applying the statute's standards to decide if appellant should have been licensed. Because appellant had an adversarial hearing, focusing on his need and fitness for such a firearms license, appellant's constitutionally protected right to bear arms was not violated. The court also held that because the Pennsylvania Uniform Firearms Act, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6110 named certain persons, such as habitual drunkards, persons of unsound mind, and persons convicted of a crime of violence, ineligible to carry a firearm, the sheriff was not limited to denying firearms licenses only to such persons.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed because appellee sheriff's denial of a firearms license to appellant was soundly based upon the need and suitability criteria of the Firearms Act.

Dithridge House Asso. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


No. 1402 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


116 Pa. Commw. 24; 541 A.2d 827; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 351


March 22, 1988, Argued  
May 6, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Association granted leave to withdraw application for permit.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Environmental Hearing Board, in the case of Dithridge House Association v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources, EHB Docket No. 86-550-R, dated June 17, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant challenged the determination of respondent Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), which granted summary affirmance of a state agency's denial of petitioner's application for a public bathing plan permit pursuant to 25 Pa. Code § 193.14 for a pool in its condominium complex and request to withdraw the application upon discovery that condominium pools were exempt from the permit requirement under an amendment to § 193.14.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner applicant built a swimming pool inside its condominium complex. Its contractor applied for a public bathing plan permit under Pa. Code § 193.14, which was denied by respondent Environmental Hearing Board. Neither petitioner nor the contractor appealed the decision. Later, § 193.14 was amended to exclude condominium pools from the permit requirement. Six years thereafter, petitioner applied for a permit, but requested to withdraw its application. Respondent granted summary judgment for the state agency in affirming the denial of a permit and request to withdraw. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and held that issue preclusion did not bar petitioner from challenging the decision because of the intervening change in the legal context exception. Petitioner could not have litigated the amendment to the permit requirement because its present claim of a valid legal status for a permit was different from its claim prior to the amendment. Inequitable administration of the law would result if petitioner were precluded, on an administrative finality, from arguing the permit requirement no longer applied to it while similarly situated persons would not be precluded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed respondent Environmental Hearing Board's summary affirmance of the state agency's denial of petitioner applicant's request for a public bathing plan permit for its condominium pool and to withdraw its application. Petitioner was not estopped under the doctrine of issue preclusion to challenge the amendment exempting condominium pools from the permit requirement because of the intervening change in the legal context exception.

Bartholomew on behalf of Bartholomew v. Foster

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


115 Pa. Commw. 430; 541 A.2d 393; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 353


November 18, 1987, Argued  
April 25, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Ann and Craig Bartholomew, on behalf of their son, Jonathan Bartholomew, and The League of Women Voters of Pennsylvania, on behalf of its members v. Constance B. Foster, in her official capacity as Commissioner of the Pennsylvania Insurance Department.

I, § 28 and further enjoining respondent insurance commissioner from otherwise enforcing § 1183(e). Respondent sought a contrary declaration and contended that § 1183(e) was constitutional because the gender-based insurance rates charged by the respective companies were founded upon sound actuarial principles.

The court reasoned that all other types of sexual discrimination had been outlawed in the commonwealth. The court further reasoned that the ability to operate a motor vehicle was not a physical characteristic uniquely related to one's sex. The court concluded that sex-based gender classifications pertaining to insurance rates was unconstitutional. The court held that that such disparate treatment violated the Pennsylvania Constitution. Summary judgment was granted in favor of petitioners and denied to respondents.

Respondent's cross-motion for summary judgment was denied. The court held that sex-based gender classification pertaining to insurance rates were unconstitutional.

King v. Breach


No. 76 T.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


115 Pa. Commw. 355; 540 A.2d 976; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 234


November 17, 1987, Submitted on Briefs  
April 15, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, in the case of Carol T. King and David A. King, Sr., her husband v. Carol Breach, Edward Russek, M.D., Dennis Philbin, individually and as Deputy Warden for Treatment Services for Dauphin County Prison, Dauphin County Prison, Stanley Mrozowski, individually and as County Administrator of Dauphin County Mental Health and Mental Retardation Program, and Dauphin County Mental Health and Mental Retardation Program, No. 3328 S 1985, dated August 18, 1986.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, wife and husband, challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, prison, deputy warden, county mental health and retardation program, and administrator, in an action for damages for injuries appellant wife sustained while carrying out her duties as a psychiatric nurse at a state hospital when she was assaulted by appellee inmate.


OVERVIEW: Appellant wife, a psychiatric nurse at a state hospital, was assaulted by appellee inmate, and appellants, wife and husband, filed a complaint against appellees, inmate, prison, deputy warden, county mental health program, and administrator, for willful misconduct and negligence. The trial court entered summary judgment for appellees, holding that agencies were immune under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8541. The court agreed, holding that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8550 only abolished immunity for willful misconduct of local agency employees and did not affect agency immunity. Appellees, prison and county mental health program, were immune under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8542, and actions against them were barred by § 8541. 50 P.S. § 7114, which provided a limited abolition of immunity, was repealed by 53 P.S. § 5311.802(c) of the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act. The court held that appellees, deputy warden and administrator, could be liable, but that the allegations did not support a conclusion that they knew that the assault was a substantially certain result of their conduct, so that it could be said that they intended such a result, and the actions were barred by 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8545.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment denying appellants, wife and husband damages for injuries sustained by appellant wife when appellee inmate assaulted her. The court held that a limited abolition of immunity had been repealed and that appellants' allegations did not support a conclusion that appellees, deputy warden and administrator, knew that the assault was a substantially certain result of their conduct.
