Parker v. Commonwealth


No. 583 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


115 Pa. Commw. 93; 540 A.2d 313; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 216


June 8, 1987, Argued  
March 31, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Pearlie M. Parker, Richard W. Bittinger, Wayne Stine and Leonard Spielman, on behalf of themselves and all others similarly situated v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Labor and Industry and Harris L. Wofford, Jr., Secretary of Labor and Industry, and Knouse Foods Cooperative, Inc., Motts U.S.A., W. E. Bittinger Co., Inc., John F. Cope Co., Inc., Furman Foods, Inc., Benjamin Lipitz Co., Kresge Farm Foods, Inc., and Welch Foods, Inc.



DISPOSITION: Petition for review dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, government and private companies, filed preliminary objections in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania, demurring to petitioners, class of seasonal workers', action seeking a judgment declaring the Unemployment Compensation Law (Law), 43 P.S. § 802.5 unconstitutional. Petitioners also sought an injunction against further application of the Law.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, class of seasonal workers, sought to have Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 P.S. § 802.5, declared unconstitutional, and sought an injunction against further application of the § 802.5, which provided that unemployment compensation benefits would not be paid to seasonal workers during the off-season. Respondents, government and private companies, demurred to the complaint. The court sustained the demurrers and dismissed petitioners' action. The Declaratory Judgment Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7541(c), provided jurisdiction as constitutional claims were raised, but not over respondent private companies that did not employ petitioners. The court held that U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Pa. Const. art. III, § 32, were not violated as the classification of seasonal workers was rationally related to a legitimate state end. Pa. Const. art. III, § 1 was not violated as public was put on notice as to the intent of § 802.5 during the legislative process. Petitioners' procedural due process rights were not violated by § 802.5 failing to provide for notice of an employer's seasonal determination. Such was not a final adjudication of petitioners' rights.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the demurrers of respondents, government and private companies, and dismissed petitioners, class of seasonal workers', declaratory judgment and injunctive relief action, as the Unemployment Compensation Law did not violate petitioners state constitutional, equal protection, substantive, or procedural due process rights.

 

763 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


CRH Catering Co. v. Commonwealth


No. 2630 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


114 Pa. Commw. 514; 539 A.2d 38; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 170


December 17, 1987, Argued  
March 21, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction from the order of the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania in the case of CRH Catering Co., Inc., a Pennsylvania Corporation v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, dated February 18, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Affirmed in part. Reversed in part. Additional judgment with interest entered for taxpayer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer filed exceptions to a decision of the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania, which rejected petitioner's contention that the assessment of sales tax upon certain food items dispensed by vending machine was unconstitutional. Petition argued that identical items were not taxed when purchased in a convenience store. Petitioner also challenged the court's order upholding respondent commonwealth's method of computing sales tax.


OVERVIEW: Considering objections filed by petitioner taxpayer, the court affirmed its prior ruling that petitioner did not meet its burden of proving that the assessment of sales tax on its retail sales pursuant to 72 P.S. § 7202(d)(1971) and 72 P.S. § 7204(29)(1971) was unconstitutional. Petitioner made a constitutional argument based on the imposition of sales tax on items it sold from vending machines that were identical to items not taxed sold in stores. The court held that petitioner's provision of microwave ovens and tables and chairs at certain locations permitted the categorization of petitioner's vending machines as an "other eating place" under 72 P.S. § 7204. The court found that in its merchandising and consumer base, petitioner's sales were distinguishable from those of a store so as to justify a distinctive tax burden. The court reversed its decision as to respondent commonwealth's method of calculating sales tax, invalidating 61 Pa. Code § 31.28 to the extent that it imposed tax on gross receipts collected from any machine. The court found that petitioner met its burden of proving that respondent's method of calculating sales tax imposed double taxation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed its previous determination that petitioner taxpayer did not meet its burden of proving that assessment of sales tax on its retail sales was unconstitutional, but reversed in part, finding that petitioner met its burden of proving that respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania's method of calculating sales tax resulted in double taxation.

Morris v. Commonwealth, Public School Employees' Retirement System


No. 184 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


114 Pa. Commw. 369; 538 A.2d 1385; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 156


December 18, 1987, Argued  
March 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Public School Employees' Retirement Board, in case of In Re: Claim of Sidney Morris, S.S. No. 008-10-7293.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, school teacher, sought review of an order of the Pennsylvania Public School Employees' Retirement Board (Board), which denied his appeal to retain credit in the Public School Employees' Retirement System (System) for his military service because he was eligible to receive a retirement benefit for his military service in the form of a federal civil service pension pursuant to 5 U.S.C.S. §§ 8331-8351.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, school teacher, applied for and was permitted to buy a service credit in the Public School Employees' Retirement System (System) for his 3.42 years of military service pursuant to § 8304 of the Public School Employees' Retirement Code, as amended, 24 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8304. The system later notified petitioner that he was not entitled to purchase a service credit because he was eligible to receive a retirement benefit for his military service in the form of a federal civil service pension. Petitioner appealed the determination of the Pennsylvania Public School Employees' Retirement Board that he was not entitled to the service credit. The court affirmed the board's decision and held that because credit for military service in the system was a benefit which the commonwealth need not have offered, it was a legitimate state interest to limit that benefit to individuals who could not otherwise receive a benefit for their military service. The court further held that it was not irrational for the general assembly to enact the restriction and that it was not violative of any substantive due process or equal protection rights petitioner might have had.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that petitioner, school teacher, was not entitled to purchase a credit for his years of military service because he was eligible to receive a retirement benefit for his military service in the form of a federal civil service pension. The court held that the limitation set on his purchase of a service credit by the commonwealth was rational.

Northampton, Bucks County, Municipal Authority v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


No. 2048 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


114 Pa. Commw. 339; 547 A.2d 802; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 770


December 14, 1987, Argued  
March 10, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Environmental Hearing Board in the case of Allegheny County Sanitary Authority v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources, No. 78-053-H.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner municipal authority sought review of an order from the Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), which affirmed respondent Department of Environmental Resource's determination that the construction costs for certain waste interceptors were not eligible for state subsidy under 35 P.S. §§ 701-703. Petitioner contended that 25 Pa. Code § 103.25(e)(1), which identified interceptors eligible for subsidy, was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Department of Environmental Resources concluded that not all of the construction costs for three waste interceptors built by petitioner municipal authority were eligible for subsidization under 35 P.S. § 701-703. Under 25 Pa. Code § 103.25(e)(1), interceptors which were considered integral portions of the sewage treatment works were eligible for subsidy payments. The court noted that if the intent of the legislature were to include all interceptors as eligible for subsidization, then the words "essential" and "integral" would not have been utilized. The court affirmed the order of the Environmental Hearing Board, which affirmed respondent's determination that certain waste interceptors were not eligible for state subsidy, finding that 25 Pa. Code § 103.25(e)(1) was a valid regulation, and its application was not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Environmental Hearing Board, which affirmed respondent Department of Environmental Resources' determination that waste interceptors constructed by petitioner municipal authority were not eligible for state subsidy. The court found that the code section which limited the subsidy for interceptors was a valid regulation, and its application was not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable.

Philadelphia Electric Co. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Revenue


No. 1420 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


114 Pa. Commw. 114; 538 A.2d 607; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 279


September 16, 1987, Argued  
February 29, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Philadelphia Electric Company v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Revenue and Penn Center House, Inc. and Council of 220 West Rittenhouse Square.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections overruled. Motion denied. Summary judgment entered in favor of respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner electric company filed a motion for summary judgment against respondent, state and condominiums, seeking a declaration that the prepayment provision of the Tax Reform Act of 1971, 72 P.S. § 7201(m) (1987), was unconstitutional, and seeking an order that respondent condominiums reimburse it for sales taxes it paid.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner electric company provided heat and electricity to respondent condominiums, and was required by the Tax Reform Act of 1971 (Act), 72 P.S. § 7201(m) (1987), to prepay sales taxes. Respondent condominiums claimed an exemption for residential use and refused to pay sales taxes while they awaited the outcome of litigation against respondent state. Petitioner filed an action seeking a declaration that the prepayment provision of the Act was unconstitutional, and an order for respondent condominiums to reimburse it for taxes paid on their behalf. Petitioner then filed a motion for summary judgment. The court denied petitioner's motion and entered judgment for respondents because petitioner failed to establish any tax liability on the part of respondent condominiums. Respondent condominiums never legally owed the sales taxes at issue, so petitioner made an "overpayment" and could be entitled to a refund with interest. The court found that public utilities, by virtue of being the only state regulated monopolies, had a variety of benefits not available to other business utilities, so the requirement that they prepay taxes to non-residential customers is just and reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner electric company's motion for summary judgment and entered judgment for respondent, state and condominiums, because petitioner failed to establish any tax liability on the part of respondent condominiums. The court found that because respondent condominiums never legally owed the taxes, petitioner had made an overpayment of his own taxes.

Reichley v. North Penn Sch. Dist.


No. 597 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


113 Pa. Commw. 528; 537 A.2d 391; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 310


December 16, 1987, Argued  
February 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, in case of Melissa Reichley, a minor and student, by her parent and natural guardian, Helen Wall, et al. v. North Penn School District, et al., No. 86-15062.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a minor and her parents, challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed an action for an injunction, seeking to compel striking teachers to return to work, and for declaratory relief, seeking a declaration that the Public Employee Relations Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 1101.1003 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a minor and her parents, brought suit against appellees, a school district, a teacher's union, and the commonwealth, seeking an injunction, compelling striking teachers to return to work, and seeking a declaration that the Public Employee Relations Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 1101.1003, was unconstitutional. Appellee district and appellee union filed preliminary objections, alleging lack of jurisdiction and lack of standing. The appellate court held that appellee commonwealth was not an indispensable party and that appellants had standing. The court found that the trial court improperly sustained the preliminary objections. Therefore, the court reversed the order and remanded the matter for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed an order that dismissed an injunction proceeding and a declaratory action. The court held that the trial court improperly sustained the preliminary objections, incorrectly determined that appellants, a minor and her parents, lacked standing, and incorrectly found that appellee commonwealth was an indispensable party.

The parties sought a declaration of their rights under the Pennsylvania Urban Mass Transportation Law, 55 P.S. §§ 600.100-600.407 (Supp. 1987).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner private transportation company filed an original petition for review, which sought mandamus, equity, and an action for a declaration of its rights to reimbursement for participation in the shared-ride program that was administered by respondent, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, under the Pennsylvania Urban Mass Transportation Law, 55 P.S. §§ 600.100-600.407 (Supp. 1987). Woodling v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania Bd. of Probation & Parole


No. 1609 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


113 Pa. Commw. 310; 537 A.2d 89; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 88


December 14, 1987, Submitted on Briefs  
February 8, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, in case of Ronald E. Woodling, dated June 16, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the order of the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole which recommitted him as a technical parole violator to serve backtime for violation of a special condition of his parole from convictions for statutory rape and corruption of minors.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of statutory rape and corruption of minors, and paroled upon the special condition that he not associate with minors without his parole agent's prior approval. Petitioner secured employment as the director of a play and one of the actors was a 13 year old boy. Petitioner invited the boy into his home and made a practice of transporting him to and from rehearsals in his van. Petitioner did not have his parole agent's permission to associate with the child. A warrant was issued for petitioner as a technical parole violator and he was recommitted to serve 15 months backtime. On appeal, the court affirmed and found that it was not difficult to arrive at a sure and workable meaning as to what "do not associate with minors" meant in the context of a convicted sex offender. The court concluded that the term "associate" was an ordinary term used to express ideas which found adequate interpretation in common usage and understanding, and therefore satisfied the constitutional requirement of reasonable certainty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order recommitting petitioner for violation of special condition of parole. The court found that the special condition was not vague because the term "associate" had a common usage and understanding, and thus satisfied the constitutional requirement of reasonable certainty.

Upper Gwynedd Township Authority v. Roth


Nos. 2735 C.D. 1986, 2736 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


113 Pa. Commw. 239; 536 A.2d 875; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 121


June 8, 1987, Argued  
February 3, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for reargument filed and denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County in the case of Upper Gwynedd Township Authority v. Abraham and Edythe Roth, Nos. 82-03333 and 82-03352.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which was entered in favor of appellee township authority on its municipal claims against appellant's land and which denied her motions for a new trial or judgment non obstante veredicto.


OVERVIEW: Appellee township authority passed a resolution authorizing the construction of a sanitary sewer system along the street where appellant property owner's two tracts of land were located. After the completion of the sewer system, appellee filed municipal claims against appellant's two tracts. Appellant challenged that assessment. The trial court found the sewer assessments valid and proper, and denied appellant's motions for post-trial relief. Appellant challenged the trial court's judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. Appellee liens were not time-barred even though appellee filed the liens some nine years after construction of the sewer project was completed. Pursuant to 53 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7432, there are no time limitations on the filing of municipal claims. The court rejected appellant's argument that the imposition of liens on her property pursuant to the validation statute was unconstitutional and deprived her of due process. Also, the court held that appellant failed to rebut the presumption that the sewer line benefitted her property. Finally, as substantial evidence showed that appellant's property was urban in character, assessment by the front-foot method was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which was entered in favor of appellee township on its municipal claims against appellant property owner's land, and which denied appellant's post-trial motions. The municipal liens were timely filed, appellant's property was benefitted by the sewer line at issue, and appellant's property was properly assessed by the front-foot method as evidence showed that the property was urban in character.

Trinity Lutheran Evangelical Church v. May ex rel. W. Pennsylvania-West Va. Synod of the Lutheran Church in Am.


No. 30 T.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


112 Pa. Commw. 557; 537 A.2d 38; 1988 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 47


October 7, 1987, Argued  
January 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, in case of Bishop Kenneth R. May, on behalf of The Western Pennsylvania-West Virginia Synod of The Lutheran Church in America, a corporation v. Trinity Lutheran Evangelical Church, a non-profit corporation, and Rev. D. Douglas Roth, Wayne Cochran, Harry Dinkel, William Fosbrink, Nadine Roth, Joann Reilly, Helve Gogots, Rebecca Fosbrink and Marian Welshham, individuals, No. GD 84-21773, dated September 17, 1986.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant church sought review of an equitable decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), making permanent a preliminary injunction ordering defendant church to turn over all church property to plaintiff synod and to refrain from interfering with plaintiff's use of the property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant church challenged the trial court's order permanently enjoining defendant from interfering with plaintiff synod's use of local church property. Defendant pastor and church council had a serious doctrinal dispute with plaintiff, resulting in plaintiff's removal of the pastor under church by-laws. Church council members transferred money from defendant's bank account into their personal accounts and had to be forcibly removed from the church by the sheriff. When council members refused to obey the preliminary injunction, they were held in contempt and jailed. On appeal, the court held that defendant council members were not denied their right to a speedy trial because the contempt order was civil in nature and could be purged by obeying the preliminary injunction. As long as plaintiff had followed its own internal rules, the trial court had jurisdiction to adjudicate under U.S. Const. amend. I because the parties' property dispute was contractual in nature. The court vacated the permanent injunction and remanded for determination of whether plaintiff had followed its own rules prior to the injunction's being made permanent. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order holding defendant church council members in contempt for failing to obey a preliminary injunction ordering them to turn over church property to plaintiff synod. The trial court had jurisdiction to hear the dispute, which was grounded in contract rather than in ecclesiastical law, as long as plaintiff had followed its own internal procedures. The court vacated the permanent injunction and remanded.

Broadwood Chuckwagon v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Bd. (Stovall)


No. 3355 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


112 Pa. Commw. 213; 535 A.2d 272; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2751


February 26, 1987, Argued  
December 29, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued September 16, 1987. Application for Reargument Filed and Denied. (74 Pa. Commonwealth Ct. 426). Reargument Granted May 28, 1987, Regarding Continuance of Benefits to Minor Dependent.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board, in the case of Kenneth Stovall, Deceased, Marion Stovall, Mother v. Broadwood Chuckwagon, No. A-87509.



DISPOSITION: Modified and remanded. Board order of November 15, 1985 reversed. Case remanded for computation of benefits based on dependency from time of decedent's death until claimant's minor child's eighteenth birthday.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania) which had been modified on remand for a determination of dependency benefits. The court granted reargument of the matter, limited to the issue of whether, pursuant decisional case law, claimant mother's benefits should have terminated when her child reached the age of 18.


OVERVIEW: At issue on reargument was whether claimant mother's dependency benefits should terminate when her child reached the age of 18. It had previously been determined by the court that claimant, whose son was killed by a co-employee, had established the requisite dependency to be entitled to benefits under the Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act (Act), 77 P.S. § 561(5). Because claimant was obligated to support her minor children, the amount of the decedent's contribution attributable to the minor sister's college tuition was a necessity of life, but only until the decedent's sister reached the age of 18 years. Here, the court reversed the order of the workmen's compensation board and remanded the case for computation of benefits for dependency from the time of decedent's death until claimant's minor child's 18th birthday, under 77 P.S. § 562, because the determination of dependency, subject to a subsequent condition, comported with the overall objective of the Act, which was to compensate persons who were actually dependent to some extent upon a deceased worker whose death was work-related.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order of the workmen's compensation board because claimant mother's argument that statutory silence as to any durational limit compelled the interpretation that dependent parents were entitled to benefits until they died was rejected. The court found that claimant's dependency existed on account of the educational expenses of decedent's minor sister, and that the obligation terminated when the child reached 18.

City of Pittsburgh v. Commonwealth


No. 3293 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


112 Pa. Commw. 188; 535 A.2d 680; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2750


October 7, 1987, Argued  
December 24, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Modification of Order Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Jurisdiction in the case of City of Pittsburgh, a municipal corporation, and Richard S. Caliguiri, an individual and Mayor, City of Pittsburgh v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and James I. Scheiner, Secretary of Revenue, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Respondents' preliminary objections sustained. City of Pittsburgh removed as petitioner. Governor and Secretary of Revenue removed from case. Respondents' motion to strike sustained. Petitioner's application for summary relief denied. Commonwealth granted thirty days to file answer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, city and mayor, sough injunctive relief and declaratory judgment relief from the court (Pennsylvania). Petitioners requested that the court declare unconstitutional a portion of the Local Tax Enabling Act, 53 P.S. § 6914 and a section of the Home Rule Charter and Optional Plans Law, 53 P.S. § 1-303(a)(7).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner city imposed a tax on the salaries, wages, commissions and other compensation earned by both residents and non-residents for work done or services performed in petitioner city. The Local Tax Enabling act, 53 P.S. § 6914 and the Home Rule Charter and Optional Plans La, 53 P.S. § 1-303(a)(7) established rules for levying taxes on non-residents, which petitioners, city and mayor, believed place an unfair burden on it citizens. The court issued respondent commonwealth, governor, and secretary's demurrer as to the constitutional challenges because petitioner city had no standing to assert the claims of its citizens against the commonwealth. The court ordered respondent governor removed from the suit because respondent governor was not the appropriate party. Respondent secretary was removed because this cause of action was not concerned with a state taxing statute. The court found that the treatment of residents and non-residents was not unconstitutional when § 6914 merely credited non-residents with any tax that they may have paid to another political subdivisions. In this respect, all persons are paying the same tax.


OUTCOME: Court sustained respondents' preliminary objections because petitioner city had no standing to assert claims of citizens against respondent commonwealth. Petitioner city was removed as petitioner and respondent governor and secretary were removed as respondents as they were improper parties. Respondent commonwealth was granted leave to file an answer for review with respect to a constitutional challenge asserted by petitioner mayor.

Stanley v. Department of Pub. Welfare


No. 1494 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


112 Pa. Commw. 157; 535 A.2d 674; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2712


June 12, 1987, Argued  
December 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Public Welfare in the case of Appeal of: Debbie Stanley, Case No. 67-0088722.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order by respondent Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a hearing examiner's decision denying petitioner medical assistance benefits on behalf of her newborn son.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner applied for medical assistance benefits for her infant son. Respondent department's local office requested financial information and income verification to determine eligibility. The local office denied assistance when neither petitioner nor her husband responded with the appropriate information. The court affirmed the order of respondent because the regulations relied upon clearly required petitioner to substantiate her financial status in support of a medical assistance application under 55 Pa. Code, § 125.84(c)-(e). As petitioner failed to do so, the court concluded that her application was properly denied. The court found that the parents of an infant child were responsible for the costs incurred and must be considered the medical assistance applicants of any request assistance. The court found that petitioner was not entitled to interim award because the local office failed to act on petitioner's application in a timely fashion. The court held that petitioner's reliance on 62 P.S. § 432.19 was in error because this section pertained to assistance other than medical assistance. Also there was no mandate for an interim award authorized on the basis of an application.


OUTCOME: Respondent department's order denying petitioner medical assistance benefits was affirmed because the court found that regulations relied on clearly required petitioner to substantiate financial status which she failed to do. The court found that petitioner was not entitled to interim award because it was not mandatory and regulation was reasonable that information may be more difficult to obtain from absents parents than form an intact family.

City of Philadelphia v. District Council 33


No. 591 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


112 Pa. Commw. 90; 535 A.2d 231; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2706


September 16, 1987, Argued  
December 18, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, in case of District Council 33, et al. v. City of Philadelphia, No. 2118, January Term, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Lower court order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) which preliminarily enjoined appellant from enforcing a city ordinance that purported to establish a pension plan for new city employees different from the plan provided in the collective bargaining agreement between appellant and appellee union, the exclusive bargaining representative for most of appellant's civil service employees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city challenged a preliminary injunction which enjoined it from enforcing an ordinance that was passed to comply with provisions of the Municipal Pension Plan Funding Standard and Recovery Act, 53 P.S. §§ 895.101-895.803. The ordinance purported to establish a pension plan for new city employees different from the plan provided in the collective bargaining agreement between appellant and appellee union. On appeal, the court ruled that the nature of appellee's claim was an action to enforce the contract; therefore, the trial court properly had jurisdiction. Because the preliminary injunction at issue was prohibitory, the court reviewed the grant of the injunction under the apparently reasonable grounds standard. Although the trial judge's conclusion of irreparable harm was based primarily on inference, the court did not find that it was supported by no apparently reasonable basis. The issue of possible adverse effect on the public interest was not disregarded below; the lower court provided that the injunction might be dissolved upon a showing by the city that the continued enforcement of the injunction would be more harmful than dissolution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the preliminary injunction which enjoined appellant city from enforcing a city ordinance which established a pension plan for new city employees different from the plan provided in the collective bargaining agreement between appellant and appellee union. The court reviewed the injunction under the "apparently reasonable grounds" standard.

 

776 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Charter Hospital of Bucks County, Inc. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Health


No. 343 Miscellaneous Docket No. 4


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


111 Pa. Commw. 576; 534 A.2d 1125; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2690


September 15, 1987, Argued  
December 11, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Health Facility Hearing Board in the case of In Re: Charter House Hospital of Bucks County, Pennsylvania, Inc.; Project Nos.: CON-86-A-6517-B; CON-86-C-6518-B; CON-86-H-6519-B; Docket Nos. CN 87-001, CN 87-002, CN 87-003, dated May 29, 1987.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought relief from an order of the State Health Facility Hearing Board (Pennsylvania), upholding the Pennsylvania Department of Health's determination that the psychiatric hospitals proposed by appellant were subject to certificate-of-need review pursuant to 35 P.S. § 448.101 of the Health Care Facilities Act. Appellant asserted that its projects were excluded from certificate-of-need review under 35 PS. § 448.103.


OVERVIEW: Proposing a hospital project which accepted no federal or state funds, appellant hospital requested a non-reviewability determination pursuant to 35 P.S. § 446.103. On appeal, the court held that under the amended language of 42 U.S.C.S. § 300m-2, the self-destructing clause of § 446.103 was triggered when the exclusionary provision became inconsistent with the federal regulations established by the federal Secretary of Health and Human Services. Accordingly, respondent correctly wrote its regulations treating the exclusionary provision as if it had no effect, and its determination that appellant's proposed hospital projects were subject to certificate-of-need review was proper and in accord with both state and federal statute and regulations. Determining that the delegation in § 446.103 fit the definition of a status-finding type statute, the court held that the statute did not unlawfully delegate state legislative authority to the federal Secretary in violation of Pa. Const. art. II, § 1, but merely requested a determination of whether the exclusionary provision conformed to the established federal program.


OUTCOME: Decision of the State Health Facility Hearing Board holding that projects proposed by appellant hospital were subject to certificate-of-need review under the Health Care Facilities Act was affirmed as the statutory exclusion provision was void as being inconsistent with federal guidelines and the requirement that the statute conform to the federal program was not an unconstitutional delegation of law-making.

 

777 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Scalzi v. Altoona


No. 2634 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


111 Pa. Commw. 479; 533 A.2d 1150; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2670


October 5, 1987, Argued  
December 4, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied September 21, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Blair County in the case of Rocco Scalzi v. City of Altoona, No. 88 C.P. 1984.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Blair County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his appeal from a determination by appellee city's council to remove him from his position. Appellant contended that the mayor's dual roles as the one who preferred the charges against appellant and who also chaired the council hearing that resulted in appellant's dismissal violated appellant's due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officer had charges of misconduct preferred against him by the mayor of appellee city, pursuant to the authority conferred by 53 P.S. § 36103. Thereafter the mayor, in accordance with § 36103, sat as a member of appellee's council that conducted the hearing resulting in appellant's dismissal. The trial court dismissed the appeal, and appellant sought further review, contending that an impermissible commingling of the prosecutorial and adjudicatory functions of the mayor resulted in a violation of appellant's due process rights. The court reversed the decision and remanded the cause for a new hearing before appellee's council without the participation of the mayor. The court found that, while the statutory scheme established the potential for a due process violation because of the commingling of the mayor's prosecutorial and adjudicatory functions, the statutes did not require the mayor to sit in the adjudication of the charges but required only that he be the one who preferred the charges. The court concluded that the mayor should have recused himself from the due process hearing and that his failure to do so violated appellant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision that affirmed the action of appellee city's council that dismissed appellant police officer from his position. The court found that, while the mayor was responsible for preferring the charges against appellant, the statutory scheme did not require the mayor to sit in adjudication of the matter, and his doing so violated appellant's right to due process.

Mellinger v. Commonwealth


Nos. 963 C.D. 1986, 254 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


111 Pa. Commw. 377; 533 A.2d 1119; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2649


September 15, 1987, Argued  
December 1, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Department of Community Affairs in the case of In Re: Annville-Cleona School District, $ 2,950,000 General Obligation Bonds, William B. Mellinger, Joerg W. P. Mayer, and Ruth C. Beachler v. Annville-Cleona School District, Lebanon County, Pennsylvania, Docket No. LGUDA-25; and in the case of In Re: Annville-Cleona School District, Dennis R. Marshall, et al., and Annville-Cleona Taxation Advisory Committee v. Annville-Cleona School District, Lebanon County, Pennsylvania, Docket No. LGUDA-27.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers sought review of orders from respondent, the Department of Community Affairs (Pennsylvania), which dismissed their complaints challenging two proposed bond issues by respondent school district. The petitions were consolidated for the court's consideration.


OVERVIEW: Respondent school district (district) proposed two bond issues. Petitioners filed complaints challenging those bond issues as invalid, which respondent department (department) dismissed. On review, the court held that the Local Government Unit Debt Act § 202, 53 P.S. § 6780-52, was controlling with regard to the appropriate limits of the district's non-electoral debt. Pursuant to the limits set by 53 P.S. § 6780-52, the district could properly increase its debt in the proposed amounts without first seeking the approval of the electorate. Thus, petitioners' challenge to the district's proposed increase in non-electoral bonded indebtedness was properly rejected by the department. The court also held that the department's procedure was proper and in accord with applicable rules, and given the district's admission of all material facts alleged by petitioners, evidentiary hearings were not in order; petitioners' procedural challenge was thus rejected. The court also held that the renovation of an elementary school was clearly a legitimate purpose underlying the district's decision to issue the bonds. The orders of the department were thus affirmed.


OUTCOME: Orders by respondent department dismissing petitioners' complaints, which challenged two proposed bond issues by respondent school district (district), were affirmed. Respondent district could increase its debt without first seeking approval from the electorate, respondent department's procedure was proper and evidentiary hearings were not needed, and a legitimate purpose supported respondent district's decision to issue the bonds.

Pa. Gamefowl Breeders Asso v. Commonwealth


No. 917 C.D. 1987


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


533 A.2d 838; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2646


Argued: October 9, 1987  
November 25, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Dismissed December 8, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION FOR REVIEW IN THE NATURE OF DECLARATORY JUDGMENT AND INJUNCTIVE RELIEF (NOTICE TO PLEAD)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, members of the Pennsylvania Gamefowl Breeders Association, sought review in the nature of a declaratory judgment seeking a determination that certain provisions contained in § 5511 of the Crimes Code, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511, were unconstitutional under the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions. The commonwealth filed preliminary objections and thereby sought dismissal of the petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, who were members of the Pennsylvania Gamefowl Breeders Association (association), sought review in the nature of a declaratory judgment in which they sought a determination that certain provisions contained in § 5511 of the Crimes Code, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511, were unconstitutional under the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions. Particularly, petitioners claimed that the statutes impinge upon their constitutional rights to own gamecocks and to associate with members of organizations in other states where cock fighting was legal. The court dismissed the petition on the commonwealth's preliminary objections. The court ruled that there was no allegation that any members of the association had been prosecuted or threatened with prosecution under the statute in question. Therefore, the court ruled, the events that would have given rise to a case or controversy had not occurred and may never occur. A declaratory judgment based upon such remote speculation that prosecution may occur in the future, the court ruled, was premature. The court held that petitioners did not have standing to seek relief in the nature of a declaratory judgment.


OUTCOME: The court granted the commonwealth's preliminary objections and thereby dismissed a petition for review filed by members of the Pennsylvania Gamefowl Breeders Association (petitioners). Because there was no allegation or proof that petitioners or any other member had been prosecuted or threatened with prosecution under the challenged statute, petitioners lacked standing to seek relief in the nature of a declaratory judgment.

American Federation of State, etc. v. Commonwealth


Nos. 2064 C.D. 1983, 2133 C.D. 1983, 2160 C.D. 1983


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


111 Pa. Commw. 81; 533 A.2d 785; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2614


June 10, 1987, Argued  
November 12, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in case of American Federation of State, County and Municipal Employees, AFL-CIO, by its Trustee Ad Litem, Edward J. Keller v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, The Honorable Richard Thornburgh, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; State Employees' Retirement Board, Robert L. Cusma, Executive Director of the State Employees' Retirement Board, and R. Budd Dwyer, Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; in case of Joint Bargaining Committee of the Pennsylvania Social Services Union and Pennsylvania Employment Security Employees' Association, Locals 668 and 675, SEIU, AFL-CIO, by its Trustee Ad Litem, Andrew L. Stern and Harry Beshgetoorian; Pennsylvania Social Services Union, by its Trustee Ad Litem, Andrew L. Stern; Frank Catanese, individually and on behalf of others similarly situated and Lillian Swartz, individually and on behalf of others similarly situated v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, The Honorable Richard Thornburgh, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, et al., and in case of Dennis J. Solecki and Lea F. Barbush, as individuals, on behalf of themselves and all others similarly situated v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, The Honorable [***2] Richard Thornburgh, Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania et al.



DISPOSITION: Partial summary judgment granted to petitioners. Partial summary judgment granted to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state, county and municipal employees, brought a motion for summary judgment to enforce an order that prohibited respondent state employees' retirement board from the collection of pension contributions at a rate exceeding five percent.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state employees' retirement board was enjoined from collecting pension contributions from petitioners, state, county and municipality employees, in excess of a five percent basic contribution rate. Respondent issued a directive mandating the collection of pension contributions over six percent from employees who were members of the retirement system prior to the enactment of 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5505.1(the Act), but who had been separated from employment for more than fourteen days and then reinstated. Petitioners contended that the retirement contract was controlled by the State Employees' Retirement Code, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5101-5956, which stated that membership could not be linked to continuous employment and the court agreed. As a result, the court granted partial summary judgment to petitioners and held that its prior order applied to all employees who were members before the Act and left their contributions in the retirement fund. However, the court also granted partial summary judgment to respondent and held that employees who had withdrawn their accumulated contributions, but subsequently repurchased credits, were not covered by its prior order.


OUTCOME: The court granted partial summary judgment to petitioners, state, county and municipality employees, and prohibited respondent state employees' retirement board from collecting pension contributions in excess of five percent from employees that were separated from employment prior to the enactment of the applicable statute but who had left contributions in the fund.

Barr v. Commonwealth, State Real Estate Com.

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


110 Pa. Commw. 530; 532 A.2d 1236; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2739


September 14, 1987, Argued  
October 29, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in case of David S. Barr, an individual, and 21st Century Appraisals, Inc., a Pennsylvania corporation v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Real Estate Commission.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objection relating to jurisdiction sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner real estate appraisers sought an injunction to keep respondent, Pennsylvania State Real Estate Commission, from enforcement of the Real Estate Licensing and Registration Act (Act), 63 P.S. §§ 455.101-455.902, and a declaratory judgment that the Act did not apply to them.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, Pennsylvania State Real Estate Commission, charged petitioner real estate appraisers with violating the Real Estate Licensing and Registration Act (Act), 63 P.S. §§ 455.101-455.902. Petitioners filed a petition to have the court enjoin respondent from enforcement of the Act and to have it declared unconstitutional. Respondent objected and asserted that the court lacked jurisdiction because petitioners failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. Upon review, the court agreed and stated that it did not have jurisdiction because petitioners were currently involved in a case before respondent The court stated petitioners constitutionality attack did not fall within the exception to the exhaustion of administrative remedies doctrine because the attack was to the constitutionality of the application of the Act against them and not to the unconstitutionality of it as a whole.


OUTCOME: The court sustained respondent, Pennsylvania State Real Estate Commission's, objections because it did not have jurisdiction to hear petitioner real estate appraisers' petition for an injunction and declaratory judgment because petitioners had not exhausted their administrative remedies.

Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources v. Blosenski Disposal Service


No. 205 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


110 Pa. Commw. 194; 532 A.2d 497; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2538


June 8, 1987, Argued  
October 9, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Blosenski Disposal Service, Nos. 54 and 55, 1983.



DISPOSITION: Arrest of judgment reversed. Case remanded for imposition of sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Environmental Resources sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania), which arrested judgment against appellee disposal service in an action resulting from a conviction of appellee for violation of the Solid Waste Management Act, 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6018.201 (Supp. 1987).


OVERVIEW: An employee of appellant Department of Environmental Resources entered a building without a search warrant after seeing a truck filled with trash, enter the building. The employee knew that no permit had been granted to appellee disposal service to operate the transfer station. Appellee was convicted of violations of the Solid Waste Management Act (Act), 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6018.201(Supp. 1987). Appellee filed a motion to suppress because employee entered private property without a warrant. The trial court denied the motion, holding that the waste disposal industry was so regulated that no one engaged in it had a reasonable expectation of privacy. Appellee was found guilty and his appeal was dismissed. After reconsideration, the trial court reversed its decision and held that the evidence had to be suppressed, and arrested the judgment. The court reversed the order and remanded for imposition of sentence because the agent entered the property in reliance on provisions which at the time were presumed to be constitutional. Despite the unconstitutionality of such a provision, evidence seized was nonetheless admissible because of the agent's good faith reliance on the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision in favor of appellee disposal services because the agent who entered private property without a search warrant did so in good faith reliance on his belief that he had the statutory right to do so.

Conn. General Life Ins. Co. v. Chartiers Valley Sch. Dist.


No. 2343 C.D. 1986, No. 2475 C.D. 1986, No. 2535 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


110 Pa. Commw. 171; 532 A.2d 41; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2532


May 18, 1987, Argued  
October 8, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, in case of Connecticut General Life Insurance Company, R. Gordon Mathews and Jack L. Friedlander v. Chartiers Valley School District and Township of Scott, No. GD83-14605.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which assessed penalties against them in favor of appellee taxing bodies. Appellees cross-appealed the order of the trial court that set the assessment less than the original assessment. Appellants contended that no liabilities for penalties should have attached.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers sought review of an order that assessed penalties against them in favor of appellee taxing bodies. Appellees cross-appealed an order that lowered the assessment. Appellants contended that no liabilities for penalties should have attached. The court held that 72 P.S. §5452.17 was clear and unambiguous. The court reasoned that it required a taxpayer, in order to avoid possible liability, to pay the original assessed amount. The court also held that the order became final when no one appealed. Appellants claimed that their reliance upon an order of the trial court as well as their good faith, as evidenced by both their tender and their payment into court, relieved them of any liability for penalties. The court held that the proper method would have been to pay the tax under protest and to seek a refund. The court concluded that it did not believe that reliance upon the order was a valid justification to avoid the payment of penalties. The court also held that no compound interest needed to be paid and that appellants failed to support their burden that the interest rate was unconstitutional. The orders were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The orders that assessed penalties against appellant taxpayers in favor of appellee taxing bodies and that set the assessment less than the original assessment were affirmed. The court held that appellants were required to pay the original assessed amount, that the order became final when no one appealed, and that reliance on the trial judge's order was not justification to avoid payment of the penalties.

Automobile Trade Assoc. v. Philadelphia


No. 3401 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


109 Pa. Commw. 524; 531 A.2d 573; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2480


February 25, 1987, Argued  
September 24, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, in case of Automobile Trade Association of Greater Philadelphia, et al. v. City of Philadelphia, et al., No. 2130 November Term, 1982.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, automobile dealers and their trade associations, challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that granted appellees', city and its officials, cross-motion for summary judgment, in appellants' action which sought to have the Philadelphia Mercantile License Tax declared unconstitutional as violative of Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1 and a refund of the tax paid.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, automobile dealers and their trade associations, filed a declaratory judgment action seeking to have the Philadelphia Mercantile License Tax (MLT) declared unconstitutional as violative of Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1. Appellants also sought a refund of the tax paid from 1980 through 1984. Appellants filed a motion for summary judgment. Appellees opposed the motion and filed a cross-motion for summary judgment, asserting that the constitutionality issue was moot because the MLT had been repealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the summary judgment in appellees' favor. The court found that to afford appellants relief, the trial court would have had to declare an already repealed statute to be unconstitutional, giving that decision retroactive application in order to award a refund of taxes paid. The court held that retroactive relief was discretionary and based upon the exigencies of each case. The court concluded that the trial court had not abused its discretion, in refusing appellants' request for a tax refund, because the monies in question had long since been expended on city services, and a refund would cause severe financial hardship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment to appellees, city and its officials, in action brought by appellants, car dealers and their trade associations, action, seeking to have the Philadelphia Mercantile License Tax (MLT) declared unconstitutional and a refund of the tax paid. The court noted that the MLT had been repealed and found that retroactive relief was discretionary.

Yocabet v. Commonwealth, State Ethics Com.


No. 834 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


109 Pa. Commw. 432; 531 A.2d 536; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2472


March 26, 1987, Argued  
September 18, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of State Ethics Commission No. 412-R, Issued March 3, 1986.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner township supervisor appealed from the final order of respondent State Ethics Commission (Pennsylvania), which found him in violation of the State Ethics Act, 65 P.S. § 403(a), for receiving a salary as township secretary/treasurer after he had voted to appoint himself to that position.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner township supervisor voted for his own appointment as secretary/treasurer of the township and received compensation for that position. Acting on a complaint that petitioner used his position as supervisor to realize personal financial gain, respondent State Ethics Commission issued a preliminary order in which it concluded that petitioner had violated the State Ethics Act (Act), 65 P.S. § 403(a). Petitioner challenged the order, a hearing was held, and a final order was entered finding that petitioner had violated the Act and directing him to disgorge the funds. Petitioner appealed and the court affirmed, holding that petitioner violated § 403(a), even if the additional compensation was received in good faith and without fraudulent intent. Second Class Township Code, 53 P.S. § 65101 - 66981, provided that township supervisors could appoint themselves as roadmaster, secretary, and treasurer, but that the township auditors had to set the compensation, pursuant to 53 P.S. §§ 65515 and 65531. There was substantial evidence to support respondent's finding that the auditors did not set a salary for the position of township secretary/treasurer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent State Ethics Commission that found that petitioner township supervisor had violated the State Ethics Act and that directed him to disgorge the compensation he received as the township secretary/treasurer after he had voted to appoint himself to that position, as the township auditors had not set the salary for that position.

Andrejco v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


No. 977 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


109 Pa. Commw. 389; 531 A.2d 115; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2467


April 23, 1987, Argued  
September 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Civil Service Commission in the case of John G. Andrejco v. Public Utility Commission, No. 5898.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee contested the adjudication and order of the State Civil Service Commission (Pennsylvania), which affirmed his dismissal from his employment with respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee was a public utility enforcement officer whose duties were defined by 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 307. Petitioner was discharged by respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission after it was discovered that he was the part-time employee of a regulated carrier. The court upheld his dismissal under 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 301(b), because his outside employment created a conflict of interest and was incompatible with his work for respondent. The court rejected petitioner's argument that § 301(b) was unconstitutionally void for vagueness because the term, "incompatible," as usually defined, gave a person of reasonable intelligence fair notice that his conduct would violate § 301(b), particularly where that conduct created a conflict of interest. The court found that the application of § 301(b) to petitioner was not unconstitutional because the evidence established that he was on notice that his employment with the regulated carrier was prohibited. The court held that petitioner did not disclose his outside employment to respondent and that his discharge was not too severe a penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed petitioner employee's discharge by respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission because his outside employment for a regulated carrier created a conflict of interest and was incompatible with his duties. The court held that the statute, under which petitioner was discharged, was facially valid because it gave fair notice of what constituted incompatible conduct.

Williams v. Pittsburgh

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


109 Pa. Commw. 168; 531 A.2d 42; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2435

September 4, 1987, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in the case of Betty C. Williams v. The City of Pittsburgh, Richard Caliguiri, Mayor of the City of Pittsburgh; Robert Coll, Jr., Superintendent of Police of the City of Pittsburgh; Robert Henzler, Inspector of the Number 5 Police Station, City of Pittsburgh; Harry Mulholland, Captain at the Number 5 Police Station, City of Pittsburgh; James Campbell, Detective in the Internal Affairs Section, Department of Police, City of Pittsburgh; John McGrady, Controller of the City of Pittsburgh; Pittsburgh City Council, Civil Service Commission, City of Pittsburgh, City of Pittsburgh Personnel Appeals Board, No. SA 1171-1978.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought reveiw of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County, (Pennsylvania), which affirmed appellant's discharge as a police officer by appellees, city and police department.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was employed by appellee city as a schoolteacher. During the same period of time, appellant was working for appellee as a police officer. Upon learning of appellant's dual employment, the Superintendent of Police notified appellant in a letter that her dual employment violated § 707 of appellee's Home Rule Charter. The letter concluded that failure of appellant to immediately submit a letter of resignation from the City Board of Education to the Superintendent's office, would leave him no choice but to terminate appellant. The court affirmed the discharge, holding that the Superintendent's presentation to appellant of a notice of charges and opportunity to respond before her discharge comported with constitutional guarantees of due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of appellees, city and police department, which discharged appellant employee as a police officer. The court held that appellant's discharge did not violate her constitutional guarantees of due process of law because the Superintendent of Police presented to appellant notice of charges and an opportunity to respond before her discharge.

Joint Bargaining Committee of Pennsylvania Social Services Union, Local # 668 v. Commonwealth

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in case of Joint Bargaining Committee of The Pennsylvania Social Services Union, Local # 668, SEIU and The Pennsylvania Employment Security Employees Association, Local # 675, SEIU, by its Trustee Ad Litem, Anna Burger Price and The Pennsylvania Social Services Union, Local # 668, SEIU, by its Trustee Ad Litem, Anna Burger Price v. The court granted petitioners leave to amend regarding their allegation that the auditing provision of the Pennsylvania Constitution was violated.

Montour School Dist. v. Commonwealth, Pennsylvania Human Relations Com.


No. 2307 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


109 Pa. Commw. 1; 530 A.2d 957; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2418


May 20, 1987, Argued  
August 26, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, in case of Johnnie Renner v. Montour School District, No. E-28299.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner school district sought review of an order from respondent, the Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, which adopted the recommendations, opinion, and conclusions of a hearing examiner. The examiner determined that claimant bus driver, who was forced to retire at age 70, had been discriminated against by petitioner on the basis of his age in violation of the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act, 43 P.S. § 955(a).


OVERVIEW: Claimant school bus driver filed an age discrimination action under the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act (Act), 43 P.S. § 955(a), against petitioner school district after he was forced to retire at age 70, even though he had an excellent performance record and was able to perform his job duties. The court found that claimant fell within the Act's protected class because the Act encompassed individuals through and including age 70. The court concluded that petitioner was provided with an adequate opportunity to present its defense, which was rejected as not being credible. The court disagreed with petitioner's contention that the hearing procedures violated due process because the same agency both prosecuted and adjudicated the matter. The court affirmed the decision of respondent Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, which adopted the recommendations of a hearing examiner, who determined that claimant had been discriminated against by petitioner on the basis of his age. The court held that constitutional provisions were not necessarily offended where two employees of the same agency worked in separate branches of the agency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, which adopted a hearing examiner's recommendations, who determined that claimant bus driver was discriminated against by petitioner school district on the basis of his age. The court held that claimant fell within the protected class, and the hearing process did not violate due process.

 

790 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Lyman v. Philadelphia


No. 3241 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


108 Pa. Commw. 494; 529 A.2d 1194; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2385


June 8, 1987, Argued  
August 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in the case of Cletus P. Lyman, Richard A. Ash, and Sixteen Twelve Latimer Partners v. City of Philadelphia and School District of Philadelphia, No. 2025, May Term, 1985.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorneys sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed their declaratory judgment complaint, in regard to their contention that certain provisions of the Philadelphia Code that imposed business and mercantile taxes and licenses were unconstitutional as applied to attorneys, based on appellants' failure to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorneys filed a complaint in the court of common pleas seeking declaratory relief upon their contention that certain provisions of the Philadelphia Code that imposed business and mercantile taxes and licenses were unconstitutional as applied to attorneys. The court of common pleas denied such relief on the ground that appellants had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. On review, the court reversed the lower court and remanded for further proceedings. The court noted that appellants were challenging the constitutionality of the tax and licensing enabling legislation. The court found that administrative agencies did not possess the authority to pass upon the validity and constitutionality of acts of the general assembly. Thus, the court concluded that the City's Board of License and Inspection Review and the Tax Review Board could not grant appellants the relief sought. The court ruled, therefore, that the existence of administrative remedies in the challenged ordinances did not deprive a court of its equity jurisdiction to entertain constitutional challenges to the statute itself through a declaratory judgment action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order, which had denied appellant attorneys' declaratory relief upon their contention that certain provisions of the Philadelphia Code were unconstitutional. The court ruled that the existence of administrative remedies in the challenged ordinances did not deprive a court of its equity jurisdiction to entertain constitutional challenges to the applicable statute through a declaratory judgment action.

 

791 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Insurance Adjustment Bureau v. Insurance Comm'r for Commonwealth


No. 611 C.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


108 Pa. Commw. 418; 530 A.2d 132; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2384


February 27, 1987 Argued  
August 13, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed and Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Jurisdiction in the case of Insurance Adjustment Bureau v. The Insurance Commissioner for the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objection overruled. Respondent directed to file answer within thirty days. (86 Pa. Commonwealth Court 492) Motion for summary judgment seeking permanent injunction filed by Insurance Adjustment Bureau against Insurance Commissioner. Motion for summary judgment denied. Judgment in favor of Insurance Commissioner.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought to enjoin the Insurance Commissioner of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania from enforcing the 24-hour rule, which prohibited insurance adjusters from soliciting employment from a victim within 24 hours of a loss, arguing that the rule abridged its freedom of speech.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner challenged the rule that prohibited public insurance adjusters or public insurance adjuster solicitors from soliciting employment from a victim of a loss within a 24-hour period of a fire or other catastrophe or occurrence that gave rise to the loss. Petitioner argued that the rule abridged its freedom of speech. The court denied petitioner's motion for summary judgment that sought a permanent injunction and a declaration from the court that the 24-hour rule was unconstitutional, because the rule did not violate petitioner's right to: (1) freedom of speech under both the federal and state constitutions; (2) equal protection under the laws; and (3) substantive due process. In addition, the language of the rule was not unconstitutionally vague. Therefore, the court dissolved its previous order that preliminarily enjoined enforcement of the rule.


OUTCOME: The court held in favor of respondent because the 24-hour rule did not unconstitutionally prohibit petitioner from soliciting employment as an insurance adjuster from a victim of a loss within a 24-hour period of a loss. The rule did not abridge petitioner's freedom of speech.

 

792 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth by Zimmerman v. National Apartment Leasing Co.


No. 185 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


108 Pa. Commw. 300; 529 A.2d 1157; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2372


May 19, 1987, Argued  
August 10, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in the case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania by Attorney General LeRoy S. Zimmerman v. National Apartment Leasing Company a/k/a NALCO.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant apartment leasing company filed preliminary objections to plaintiff state's amended civil action in equity under the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law, 73 P.S. §§ 201-1 to 201-9.2, which fell within the court's original jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff state filed an action in equity against defendant apartment leasing company for violations of the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law (Law), 73 P.S. §§ 201-1 to 201-9.2, seeking to impose civil penalties and enjoin it from further unlawful conduct as defined by § 201-3. Plaintiff alleged that defendant was unlawfully withholding security deposits from its tenants. Defendant filed preliminary objections. The court found that the Law was not a penal statute and that the penalties provided by § 201-8 were civil as the only penalty for a judgment in favor of plaintiff was a monetary one. The court concluded that § 201-2 did not give the state the unbridled authority to determine which activities were fair and which were not. The court found that the Law was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness and that §§ 201-2 and 201-3 sufficiently apprised individuals of what was prohibited by the Law. The court found that plaintiff's amended pleading sufficiently described the unlawful practice to enable defendant to prepare a defense. The court overruled defendant's preliminary objections.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant apartment leasing company's preliminary objections, finding that the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law was not unconstitutional as it was not a penal statute, it was not vague, and it sufficiently apprised individuals of what it prohibited. The court found plaintiff state's amended pleading sufficient for defendant to prepare a defense.

 

793 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Harman v. Commonwealth, Housing Finance Agency, Homeowners' Emergency Mortg. Assistance Program


No. 685 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


108 Pa. Commw. 285; 529 A.2d 1153; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2378


June 9, 1986, Submitted on Briefs  
August 7, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Homeowners' Emergency Mortgage Assistance Program in the case of Susan W. Harman v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Housing Finance Agency, Homeowners' Emergency Mortgage Assistance Program, No. Fact 48, dated February 14, 1984.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of an order from respondent Pennsylvania Housing Finance Agency, which denied her application for assistance under the Homeowners' Emergency Assistance Program.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant filed an application with respondent Pennsylvania Housing Finance Agency (agency) for mortgage assistance through the Homeowners' Emergency Mortgage Assistance Program, which was denied as the agency concluded there was no reasonable prospect that she could resume her full mortgage payments within 36 months or pay it to maturity. On review, the court found that the Housing Finance Agency Law (Act), 35 P.S. § 1680-404c, did not unconstitutionality delegate legislative authority to the agency. The court concluded that the Act did not contain internally inconsistent requirements for obtaining mortgage assistance as a claimant could satisfy the delinquency requirements and the eligibility requirements by demonstrating a sound income history. The court reversed the agency's order, finding that the agency erred in concluding that petitioner's monthly obligations exceeded 50 percent of her monthly income created a rebuttable presumption that she could not resume full mortgage payments in 36 months and pay the mortgage in full by maturity. The court remanded for a determination of whether petitioner qualified for assistance without the rebuttable presumption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed respondent Pennsylvania Housing Finance Agency's order that denied petitioner claimant's application for mortgage assistance under the Homeowner's Emergency Assistance Program. The court found there was no rebuttable presumption under the provisions of the Housing Finance Agency Law that if a claimant's monthly obligations exceeded her monthly income, she could not resume or fulfill her mortgage payments.

 

794 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Klein v. Commonwealth, State Employees' Retirement Bd.


No. 2374 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


108 Pa. Commw. 39; 528 A.2d 1071; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2329


February 25, 1987, Argued  
July 27, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Employees' Retirement Board in case of In The Matter of: Richard B. Klein, SS No. 159-30-9618, Non-Disability Claimant, dated January 22, 1986.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant challenged the order of respondent State Employees' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania), which denied claimant's request for reinstatement to the status he held when he was first employed by the state.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant appealed the order of respondent State Employees' Retirement Board that denied his request for reinstatement when he returned to state employment to the status the that he held when he was previously employed by the state. Pursuant to 71 P.S. § 1725-208 (1959), the court found that petitioner was entitled to credit for his prior service but did not guarantee him the right to reenter the system under the same terms that existed at the time his previous employment terminated. The court found that claimant did not resume his membership into the state retirement system until after 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5306 (1974) became effective. Therefore, the court found that petitioner was properly classified under § 5306 when he returned to state employment. The court affirmed the order because claimant was given full credit for his prior service, as required by § 1725-208, and he was properly classified under the new statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent State Employees' Retirement Board that denied petitioner claimant's request for reinstatement to the status that petitioner held when he was first employed by the state. The court found that petitioner was properly given credit for his service, and was properly classified under the statute in effect when he returned to state employment.
