McClimans v. Board of Supervisors


No. 581 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


107 Pa. Commw. 542; 529 A.2d 562; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2313


March 25, 1987, Argued  
July 22, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, in case of William and Donna McClimans, James and Mabel Paige, Michael and Paul Slavin, Stanley and Bernice Babick, Albert and Florence Bober, Albert Zak, Edward Zak, Albert Presnar, Henry Presnar, Stanley D. Presnar, Jr., Edward Presnar, John P. Presnar, Medusa Cement Company and Amerikohl Land Company v. Board of Supervisors of Shenango Township, No. 118 of 1985, M.D.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a decision of appellee Board of Supervisors, denying appellants' request that it declare relevant portions of its zoning ordinance invalid and adopt appellants' proposed curative amendment. Appellants argued that the ordinance was invalid and that they therefore had a right to strip mine on the property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowners leased the right to remove, by strip mining process, coal on their property. The property was zoned for residential use and the local zoning ordinance prohibited surface mining in residential areas. Appellants filed a request for a curative amendment. Appellee board of supervisors refused to grant the curative amendment and the trial court upheld that decision. Appellants insisted that the ordinance was invalid because it did not contain a statement of objectives, regulated surface mining, totally excluded strip mining, and argued that they had a right to strip mine on the property. On appeal, the court vacated the decision of the trial court, holding that the lack of a statement of community objectives did not render the local ordinance invalid. The court stated that there was ample evidence to support appellee's findings that to permit strip mining in the residential zone would be detrimental to the public's health, safety, and general welfare. The court remanded for determination whether the ordinance prevented appellants from gaining access the their subsurface property, thus rendering the ordinance invalid as a taking without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the trial court, finding that the lack of a statement of community objectives did not render the local ordinance invalid. The court stated that if appellant landowners had proved that they were prevented by the ordinance from extracting coal from the property, the ordinance would be invalid because it effected a taking without provisions for just compensation. The court remanded for additional evidence.

Ziccardi v. Commonwealth, Dep't of General Services, Bureau of Bldgs. & Grounds


No. 2701 C.D. 1978


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


109 Pa. Commw. 628; 527 A.2d 183; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2216


February 23, 1987, Submitted on Briefs  
June 8, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsidered August 6, 1987. Application for Reargument Filed. Reconsideration Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Jurisdiction in case of Linda Ziccardi v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of General Services, Bureau of Buildings and Grounds, et al.



DISPOSITION: Motion for judgment on the pleadings granted in part and denied in part. Motion of Commonwealth for judgment on the pleadings denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pennsylvania Supreme Court remanded for disposition of defendant commonwealth's motion for judgment on the pleadings. Before the court were plaintiff's claims against defendants, commonwealth, and secretary, for violation of plaintiff's constitutional rights, and wrongful discharge. Claims against defendant union for resolution included breach of duty of fair representation, and discrimination.


OVERVIEW: On remand following appeal, the court was directed to render a decision on defendant commonwealth's motion for judgment on the pleadings. Plaintiff's petition against defendants, commonwealth, secretary, and labor union, alleged that petitioner's supervisor, on more than one occasion, urged her to purchase a ticket to a fundraiser sponsored by a political party After plaintiff refused to purchase a ticket, defendants, commonwealth and secretary, terminated her employment. Plaintiff further alleged that defendant union breached its duty of fair representation. The court held plaintiff's complaint did not support a cause of action against defendant commonwealth under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Further, sovereign immunity precluded her suit against defendant commonwealth on plaintiff's claims of violation of her federal and state constitutional rights and wrongful discharge. Therefore judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendant commonwealth was granted. The court denied defendant secretary's motion for judgment on the pleadings, finding that an evidentiary hearing was required to determine the applicability of defendant secretary's qualified official immunity.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant commonwealth's motion for judgment on the pleadings finding defendant commonwealth was not a proper defendant in a violation of civil rights action, and because the legislature had not waived sovereign immunity for claims of wrongful discharge. The court denied the motion in regards to defendant secretary because an evidentiary hearing was needed to determine whether defendant secretary had qualified immunity.

Pennsylvania Independent Petroleum Producers v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Environmental Resources


No. 1195 C.D. 1985


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


106 Pa. Commw. 72; 525 A.2d 829; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2141; 93 Oil & Gas Rep. 543


November 19, 1986, Argued  
May 11, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in the case of Pennsylvania Independent Petroleum Producers, A Non-Profit Corporation v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Environmental Resources and Nicholas De Benedictis, Secretary of Environmental Resources of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied. Judgment entered for respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner oil producers' organization filed a motion for summary judgment in its declaratory judgment cause of action against respondents, state, state department of environmental resources, and secretary of the department. Petitioner challenged the constitutionality of the 1984 Oil and Gas Act, 58 P.S. §§ 601.101-601.605.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner oil producers' organization filed a motion for summary judgment in the declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of the 1984 Oil and Gas Act (Act), 58 P.S. §§ 601.101-601.605. The court found that petitioner did not establish that any of the seven provisions of the Act cited were unconstitutional. The alleged presumption-shifting effect of 58 P.S. § 601.208(c) was too speculative to be considered, bond requirements were held not to violate the Equal Protection Clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Pa. Const. art. I, § 1, and prehearing property seizure provisions were presumed to be constitutional. The court found that petitioner did not show that entry and inspection provisions of the Act violated U.S. Const. amend. IV protections, or that reporting requirements violated rights to privacy or rights against self-incrimination under U.S. Const. amend. V. The court also held that the Act contained definite and reasonable standards for criminal enforcement of violation of the provisions, and that no unlawful commingling of legislative, judicial, and prosecutorial functions existed under the Act. The court denied the motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for summary judgment filed by petitioner oil producers' organization in the declaratory judgment action against respondents, state, state department of environmental resources, and secretary of the department. Petitioner did not establish that the cited provision of the Oil and Gas Act were unconstitutional.

 

798 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Reiter v. Commonwealth


No. 1369 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


105 Pa. Commw. 623; 525 A.2d 446; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2130


February 26, 1987, Argued  
May 5, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 16, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Acting Insurance Commissioner in the case of In Re: Sidney Reiter, t/a Rider Insurance Service, Inc., Docket No. P85-2-6.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurance agent sought review of an order by the Acting Insurance Commissioner (Pennsylvania) that suspended petitioner's license, required petitioner, among other things, to cease and desist from denying access to his business records by insurance department investigators and to pay a $ 1,000 civil penalty.


OVERVIEW: Two insurance investigators' visited petitioner insurance agent and requested inspection of certain records. The inspectors had not obtained a subpoena or search warrant and were not acting on any specific complaint regarding petitioner. Petitioner refused to grant access to the records. On a subsequent visit, petitioner offered the investigator's access to two boxes of records. The investigators declined to review these records based on their opinion that the files contained only a portion of the requested records. The court reversed the order by the commissioner because it was determined that the investigator's attempted a warrantless search of petitioner's insurance records and this was not specifically authorized by Unfair Insurance Practices Act, 40 P.S. § 1171.7. The court found no indication that the legislature had granted the investigator's a right to enter insurance business without a warrant or subpoena. The court found that the required records doctrine with regards to business records holds no privilege against warrantless searches. However, the scope of the search against petitioner was clearly not limited to its required records detailed in 31 Pa. Code § 33.29(d).


OUTCOME: Commissioner's order suspending petitioner insurance agent's license and requiring petitioner to cease and desist from denying access to his business records and to pay a $ 1,000 civil penalty was reversed because the court concluded that the investigator's attempted warrantless search of petitioner's insurance records was not authorized and petitioner may not be subjected to sanctions in objecting to the search.

 

799 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


In re Petition of Board of Directors, of Hazleton Area School Dist. etc.


No. 3107 C.D. 1986


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


105 Pa. Commw. 565; 524 A.2d 1083; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2122


April 21, 1987, Argued  
May 1, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County in the case of In Re: Petition of the Board of Directors of the Hazleton Area School District to change (re-apportion) an approved plan which established Nine Regions for election of directors within the District, No. 2314-C 1986.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant education association sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania) that, pursuant to § 303 of the Public School Code of 1949, 1949 Pa. Laws 30, as amended, 24 P.S. § 3-303, adopted a reapportionment plan that was submitted by appellee school district.


OVERVIEW: A reapportionment plan whereby a school district would be composed of nine regions was submitted by appellee school district to the lower court. The lower court adopted the plan pursuant to the provision set forth in § 303 of the Public School Code of 1949, 1949 Pa. Laws 30, as amended, 24 P.S. § 3-303, holding that the reapportionment met the all the relevant criteria, including the requirement of contiguity as set forth in § 502 of the Pennsylvania Election Code, 1937 Pa. Laws 1333, 25 P.S. § 2702. Appellant education association challenged the order. The court reversed. The court held that the apportionment plan did not meet the requirement of contiguity as required by § 502 because there were breaks in the physical territory sought to be annexed. The court disagreed with the lower court's determination that land was contiguous if it was in close proximity or near, though not in contact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order which adopted a reapportionment plan that was submitted by appellee school district, finding in favor of appellant education association. The court held that the apportionment plan could not be adopted because, due to the breaks in the land sought to be annexed by appellee, the criteria of contiguity as set forth in the Pennsylvania Election Code was not satisfied.

 

800 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Bensalem Township School Dist. v. Commonwealth


No. 1580 C.D. 1984


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


105 Pa. Commw. 388; 524 A.2d 1027; 1987 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2089


February 25, 1987, Argued  
April 22, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction in case of Bensalem Township School District, and Robert Dewey, in his own right and on behalf of all other taxpayers of Bensalem Township, and Mark Jaskolka, a minor, by Andrew Jaskolka, his parent and natural guardian, in his own right and on behalf of all other school aged children in Bensalem Township v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and The Treasurer of Pennsylvania, and The Secretary of Education of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied. Judgment entered for respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a township, a taxpayer on behalf of all other township taxpayers, and a minor on behalf of all other school aged children in the township, filed a motion for summary judgment, seeking a declaration that specific provisions of the Pennsylvania Public School Code of 1949 relating to the funding of the commonwealth's public schools were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed with the court, in its original jurisdiction, a petition for review in the nature of an action for declaratory and equitable relief against respondents (the commonwealth, the state treasurer, and the state's secretary of education), alleging that the statutory scheme for the funding of the state's public schools under the Pennsylvania Public School Code of 1949 (Code), 24 P.S. §§ 25-2502.5 and 25-2502.6, violated both the federal and state constitutions. Petitioners also sought to enjoin the distribution of subsidies to school districts. Petitioners eventually filed a motion for summary judgment. The court found that respondents' concern for maintaining an equitable distribution of the commonwealth's limited resources provided a rational basis for the Code provisions. As such, the court concluded that the provisions bore a reasonable relation to a constitutional mandate by the legislature to provide for a thorough and efficient public school system. As petitioners had not proven that the Code's funding scheme clearly, palpably, and plainly violated the Constitution, the court upheld the challenged sections and denied petitioners' motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: Petitioners' motion for summary judgment, asking for the court to declare certain provisions of the Pennsylvania Public School Code of 1949 as unconstitutional, was denied. The court found that a rational basis for such provisions, and their statutory scheme for the funding of state public schools bore a reasonable relation to a constitutional mandate by the legislature to provide for an effective and efficient public school system.
